<h1 class="firstHeading mw-first-heading" id="firstHeading"><span class="mw-page-title-main">British Empire</span></h1>
<div class="vector-body" id="bodyContent">
<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div id="contentSub2"></div>
<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>

<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#searchInput">Jump to search</a>
<div class="mw-body-content mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">States and dominions ruled by the United Kingdom</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>

class="infobox-above adr" colspan="2"><div class="ib-country-names"><div class="ib-country-name-style fn org country-name"><b>British Empire</b></div></div></th></tr><tr><td class="infobox-image" colspan="2"><div class="noresize" style="display:table; width:100%;">
<div style="display:table-cell; vertical-align:middle; padding: 0px 5px 3px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Great_Britain_(1707%E2%80%931800).svg" title="Flag of British Empire"><img alt="Flag of British Empire" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="1000" decoding="async" height="75" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Flag_of_Great_Britain_%281707%E2%80%931800%29.svg/125px-Flag_of_Great_Britain_%281707%E2%80%931800%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Flag_of_Great_Britain_%281707%E2%80%931800%29.svg/188px-Flag_of_Great_Britain_%281707%E2%80%931800%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Flag_of_Great_Britain_%281707%E2%80%931800%29.svg/250px-Flag_of_Great_Britain_%281707%E2%80%931800%29.svg.png 2x" width="125"/></a></div><div style="display:table-cell; vertical-align:middle; padding: 0px 5px 3px 0px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg"><img alt="Flag of the United Kingdom.svg" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="1200" decoding="async" height="73" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/145px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/218px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/290px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png 2x" width="145"/></a></div>
</div>
<div>Left: <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Great_Britain" title="Flag of Great Britain">Flag of Great Britain</a> (<a href="/wiki/Acts_of_Union_1707" title="Acts of Union 1707">1707–1801</a>)<br/>Right: <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Flag of the United Kingdom">Flag of the United Kingdom</a> (<a href="/wiki/Acts_of_Union_1800" title="Acts of Union 1800">1801–present</a>)</div></td></tr><tr><td class="infobox-full-data" colspan="2"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_British_Empire.png"><img alt="The British Empire.png" data-file-height="1400" data-file-width="2753" decoding="async" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/The_British_Empire.png/300px-The_British_Empire.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/The_British_Empire.png/450px-The_British_Empire.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/The_British_Empire.png/600px-The_British_Empire.png 2x" width="300"/></a><div class="ib-country-map-caption">All areas of the world that were ever part of the British Empire. Current <a href="/wiki/British_Overseas_Territories" title="British Overseas Territories">British Overseas Territories</a> have their names underlined in red.</div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The <b>British Empire</b> was composed of the <a href="/wiki/Dominion" title="Dominion">dominions</a>, <a href="/wiki/Crown_colony" title="Crown colony">colonies</a>, <a href="/wiki/Protectorate" title="Protectorate">protectorates</a>, <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations_mandate" title="League of Nations mandate">mandates</a>, and other <a href="/wiki/Dependent_territory" title="Dependent territory">territories</a> ruled or administered by the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> and its predecessor states. It began with the <a href="/wiki/English_overseas_possessions" title="English overseas possessions">overseas possessions</a> and <a href="/wiki/Trading_post" title="Trading post">trading posts</a> established by <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_England" title="Kingdom of England">England</a> between the late 16th and early 18th centuries.
At its height it was the <a href="/wiki/List_of_largest_empires" title="List of largest empires">largest empire in history</a> and, for over a century, was the foremost global power.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2004b_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2004b-1">[1]</a></sup> By 1913, the British Empire held sway over 412 million people, <span data-sort-value="7001230036515505131♠" style="display:none"></span>23 per cent of the world population at the time,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> and by 1920, it covered 35.5 million km<sup>2</sup> (13.7 million sq mi),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> <span data-sort-value="7001238351013831072♠" style="display:none"></span>24 per cent of the Earth's total land area. As a result, its <a href="/wiki/Westminster_system" title="Westminster system">constitutional</a>, <a href="/wiki/Common_law" title="Common law">legal</a>, <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">linguistic</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Culture of the United Kingdom">cultural</a> legacy is widespread. At the peak of its power, it was described as "<a href="/wiki/The_empire_on_which_the_sun_never_sets" title="The empire on which the sun never sets">the empire on which the sun never sets</a>", as the Sun was always shining on at least one of its territories.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup>
</p><p>During the <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Discovery" title="Age of Discovery">Age of Discovery</a> in the 15th and 16th centuries, <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">Portugal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spain</a> pioneered European exploration of the globe, and in the process established large overseas empires. Envious of the great wealth these empires generated,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> England, <a href="/wiki/French_colonial_empire" title="French colonial empire">France</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Empire" title="Dutch Empire">Netherlands</a> began to establish colonies and trade networks of their own in the Americas and <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a>. A series of wars in the 17th and 18th centuries with the Netherlands and France left England (<a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Great_Britain" title="Kingdom of Great Britain">Britain</a>, following the <a href="/wiki/Acts_of_Union_1707" title="Acts of Union 1707">1707 Act of Union</a> with Scotland) the dominant <a href="/wiki/Colonialism" title="Colonialism">colonial power</a> in <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North America</a>. Britain became the dominant power in the <a href="/wiki/Indian_subcontinent" title="Indian subcontinent">Indian subcontinent</a> after the <a href="/wiki/East_India_Company" title="East India Company">East India Company</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Bengal_Subah#British_colonization" title="Bengal Subah">conquest</a> of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mughal_Bengal" title="Mughal Bengal">Mughal Bengal</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Plassey" title="Battle of Plassey">Battle of Plassey</a> in 1757.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">American War of Independence</a> resulted in Britain losing some of its oldest and most populous colonies in North America by 1783. British attention then turned towards Asia, Africa, and the Pacific. After the defeat of France in the <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars" title="Napoleonic Wars">Napoleonic Wars</a> (1803–1815), Britain emerged as the principal naval and imperial power of the 19th century and expanded its imperial holdings. The period of relative peace (1815–1914) during which the British Empire became the global <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hegemon" title="Hegemon">hegemon</a> was later described as <span title="Latin-language text"><i lang="la"><a href="/wiki/Pax_Britannica" title="Pax Britannica">Pax Britannica</a></i></span> ("British Peace"). Alongside the formal control that Britain exerted over its colonies, its dominance of much of world trade meant that it effectively <a href="/wiki/Informal_empire" title="Informal empire">controlled the economies of many regions</a>, such as Asia and Latin America.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-auto-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceC_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceC-7">[7]</a></sup> Increasing degrees of autonomy were granted to its white <a href="/wiki/Settler_colonialism" title="Settler colonialism">settler colonies</a>, some of which were reclassified as <a href="/wiki/Dominion" title="Dominion">Dominions</a>.
</p><p>By the start of the 20th century, <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">Germany</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> had begun to challenge Britain's economic lead. Military and economic tensions between Britain and Germany were major causes of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/First_World_War" title="First World War">First World War</a>, during which Britain relied heavily on its empire. The conflict placed enormous strain on its military, financial, and manpower resources. Although the empire achieved its largest territorial extent immediately after the First World War, Britain was no longer the world's preeminent industrial or military power. In the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Second_World_War" title="Second World War">Second World War</a>, Britain's colonies in East Asia and Southeast Asia were occupied by the <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Japan" title="Empire of Japan">Empire of Japan</a>. Despite the final victory of Britain and <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">its allies</a>, the damage to British prestige helped accelerate the decline of the empire. <a href="/wiki/British_Raj" title="British Raj">India</a>, Britain's most valuable and populous possession, achieved <a href="/wiki/Indian_independence_movement" title="Indian independence movement">independence</a> in 1947 as part of a larger <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Decolonisation" title="Decolonisation">decolonisation</a> movement, in which Britain granted independence to most territories of the empire. The <a href="/wiki/Suez_Crisis" title="Suez Crisis">Suez Crisis</a> of 1956 confirmed Britain's decline as a global power, and the <a href="/wiki/Handover_of_Hong_Kong" title="Handover of Hong Kong">transfer of Hong Kong to China</a> on 1 July 1997 marked for many the end of the British Empire.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brendon-Empire-end_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-Brendon-Empire-end-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-refohbev594_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-refohbev594-9">[9]</a></sup> Fourteen <a href="/wiki/British_Overseas_Territories" title="British Overseas Territories">overseas territories</a> remain under British sovereignty. After independence, many former British colonies joined the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a>, a free association of independent states. Fifteen of these, including the United Kingdom, <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_realm" title="Commonwealth realm">retain a common monarch</a>, currently King <a href="/wiki/Charles_III" title="Charles III">Charles III</a>.
</p>
<div aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading" class="toc" id="toc" role="navigation"><input class="toctogglecheckbox" id="toctogglecheckbox" role="button" style="display:none" type="checkbox"/><div class="toctitle" dir="ltr" lang="en"><h2 id="mw-toc-heading">Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>

<h2><span id="Origins_.281497.E2.80.931583.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Origins_(1497–1583)">Origins (1497–1583)</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Matthew-BristolHarbour-Aug2004.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="764" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="254" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Matthew-BristolHarbour-Aug2004.jpg/170px-Matthew-BristolHarbour-Aug2004.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Matthew-BristolHarbour-Aug2004.jpg/255px-Matthew-BristolHarbour-Aug2004.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Matthew-BristolHarbour-Aug2004.jpg/340px-Matthew-BristolHarbour-Aug2004.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Matthew-BristolHarbour-Aug2004.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A replica of the <i><a href="/wiki/Matthew_(ship)" title="Matthew (ship)">Matthew</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/John_Cabot" title="John Cabot">John Cabot</a>'s ship used for his second voyage to the <a href="/wiki/New_World" title="New World">New World</a></div></div></div>
<p>The foundations of the British Empire were laid when <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_England" title="Kingdom of England">England</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Scotland" title="Kingdom of Scotland">Scotland</a> were separate kingdoms. In 1496, King <a href="/wiki/Henry_VII_of_England" title="Henry VII of England">Henry VII of England</a>, following the successes of <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spain</a> and <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">Portugal</a> in overseas exploration, commissioned <a href="/wiki/John_Cabot" title="John Cabot">John Cabot</a> to lead an expedition to discover a <a href="/wiki/Northwest_Passage" title="Northwest Passage">northwest passage</a> to Asia via the North Atlantic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2004b3_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2004b3-10">[10]</a></sup> Cabot sailed in 1497, five years after the <a href="/wiki/Voyages_of_Christopher_Columbus" title="Voyages of Christopher Columbus">first voyage of Christopher Columbus</a>, and made landfall on the coast of <a href="/wiki/Newfoundland_(island)" title="Newfoundland (island)">Newfoundland</a>. He believed he had reached Asia,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> and there was no attempt to found a colony. Cabot led another voyage to the Americas the following year but he did not return from this voyage and it is unknown what happened to his ships.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2004b4_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2004b4-12">[12]</a></sup>
</p><p>No further attempts to establish English colonies in the Americas were made until well into the <a href="/wiki/Elizabethan_era" title="Elizabethan era">reign of Queen Elizabeth I</a>, during the last decades of the 16th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> In the meantime, <a href="/wiki/Henry_VIII" title="Henry VIII">Henry VIII</a>'s 1533 <a href="/wiki/Statute_in_Restraint_of_Appeals" title="Statute in Restraint of Appeals">Statute in Restraint of Appeals</a> had declared "that this realm of England is an Empire".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/English_Reformation" title="English Reformation">Protestant Reformation</a> turned <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a> and <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic</a> Spain into implacable enemies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2004b3_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2004b3-10">[10]</a></sup> In 1562, Elizabeth I encouraged the <a href="/wiki/Privateer" title="Privateer">privateers</a> <a href="/wiki/John_Hawkins_(naval_commander)" title="John Hawkins (naval commander)">John Hawkins</a> and <a href="/wiki/Francis_Drake" title="Francis Drake">Francis Drake</a> to engage in <a href="/wiki/Slave_raiding" title="Slave raiding">slave-raiding attacks</a> against Spanish and Portuguese ships off the coast of <a href="/wiki/West_Africa" title="West Africa">West Africa</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> with the aim of establishing an <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_slave_trade" title="Atlantic slave trade">Atlantic slave trade</a>. This effort was rebuffed and later, as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anglo-Spanish_War_(1585)" title="Anglo-Spanish War (1585)">Anglo-Spanish Wars</a> intensified, <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_I" title="Elizabeth I">Elizabeth I</a> gave her blessing to further privateering raids against Spanish ports in the Americas and shipping that was returning across the Atlantic, <a href="/wiki/Spanish_treasure_fleet" title="Spanish treasure fleet">laden with treasure</a> from the <a href="/wiki/New_World" title="New World">New World</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2004b7_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2004b7-16">[16]</a></sup> At the same time, influential writers such as <a href="/wiki/Richard_Hakluyt" title="Richard Hakluyt">Richard Hakluyt</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_Dee" title="John Dee">John Dee</a> (who was the first to use the term "British Empire")<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> were beginning to press for the establishment of England's own empire. By this time, Spain had become the dominant power in the Americas and was exploring the Pacific Ocean, Portugal had established trading posts and forts from the coasts of <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a> to <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>, and France had begun to settle the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saint_Lawrence_River" title="Saint Lawrence River">Saint Lawrence River</a> area, later to become <a href="/wiki/New_France" title="New France">New France</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup>
</p><p>Although England tended to trail behind Portugal, Spain, and France in establishing overseas colonies, it carried out its first modern colonisation, referred to as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ulster_Plantation" title="Ulster Plantation">Ulster Plantation</a>, in 16th century <a href="/wiki/Ireland" title="Ireland">Ireland</a> by settling <a href="/wiki/Ulster_Protestants" title="Ulster Protestants">English Protestants</a> in <a href="/wiki/Ulster" title="Ulster">Ulster</a>. England had already colonised part of the country following the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Norman_invasion_of_Ireland" title="Norman invasion of Ireland">Norman invasion of Ireland</a> in 1169.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> Several people who helped establish the Ulster Plantations later played a part in the early colonisation of North America, particularly a group known as the <a href="/wiki/West_Country_Men" title="West Country Men">West Country Men</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span id="English_overseas_possessions_.281583.E2.80.931707.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="English_overseas_possessions_(1583–1707)">English overseas possessions (1583–1707)</span></h2>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/English_overseas_possessions" title="English overseas possessions">English overseas possessions</a></div>
<p>In 1578, Elizabeth I granted a patent to <a href="/wiki/Humphrey_Gilbert" title="Humphrey Gilbert">Humphrey Gilbert</a> for discovery and overseas exploration.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> That year, Gilbert sailed for the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a> with the intention of engaging in <a href="/wiki/Piracy" title="Piracy">piracy</a> and establishing a colony in North America, but the expedition was aborted before it had crossed the Atlantic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> In 1583, he embarked on a second attempt. On this occasion, he formally claimed the harbour of the island of Newfoundland, although no settlers were left behind. Gilbert did not survive the return journey to England and was succeeded by his half-brother, <a href="/wiki/Walter_Raleigh" title="Walter Raleigh">Walter Raleigh</a>, who was granted his own patent by Elizabeth in 1584. Later that year, Raleigh founded the <a href="/wiki/Roanoke_Colony" title="Roanoke Colony">Roanoke Colony</a> on the coast of present-day <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina" title="North Carolina">North Carolina</a>, but lack of supplies caused the colony to fail.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1603, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/James_VI_of_Scotland" title="James VI of Scotland">James VI of Scotland</a> ascended (as James I) to the English throne and in 1604 negotiated the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_London_(1604)" title="Treaty of London (1604)">Treaty of London</a>, ending hostilities with Spain. Now at peace with its main rival, English attention shifted from preying on other nations' colonial infrastructures to the business of establishing its own overseas colonies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> The British Empire began to take shape during the early 17th century, with the <a href="/wiki/British_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="British colonization of the Americas">English settlement</a> of North America and the smaller islands of the Caribbean, and the establishment of <a href="/wiki/Joint-stock_company" title="Joint-stock company">joint-stock companies</a>, most notably the <a href="/wiki/East_India_Company" title="East India Company">East India Company</a>, to administer colonies and overseas trade. This period, until the loss of the <a href="/wiki/Thirteen_Colonies" title="Thirteen Colonies">Thirteen Colonies</a> after the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">American War of Independence</a> towards the end of the 18th century, has been referred to by some historians as the "First British Empire".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Americas.2C_Africa_and_the_slave_trade"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Americas,_Africa_and_the_slave_trade">Americas, Africa and the slave trade</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_colonisation_of_the_Americas" title="British colonisation of the Americas">British colonisation of the Americas</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_America" title="British America">British America</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thirteen_Colonies" title="Thirteen Colonies">Thirteen Colonies</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_West_Indies" title="British West Indies">British West Indies</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_slave_trade" title="Atlantic slave trade">Atlantic slave trade</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tobacco_cultivation_(Virginia,_ca._1670).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="411" data-file-width="794" decoding="async" height="114" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Tobacco_cultivation_%28Virginia%2C_ca._1670%29.jpg/220px-Tobacco_cultivation_%28Virginia%2C_ca._1670%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Tobacco_cultivation_%28Virginia%2C_ca._1670%29.jpg/330px-Tobacco_cultivation_%28Virginia%2C_ca._1670%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Tobacco_cultivation_%28Virginia%2C_ca._1670%29.jpg/440px-Tobacco_cultivation_%28Virginia%2C_ca._1670%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tobacco_cultivation_(Virginia,_ca._1670).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>African slaves working in 17th-century <a href="/wiki/Colony_of_Virginia" title="Colony of Virginia">Virginia</a>, by an unknown artist, 1670</div></div></div>
<p>England's early efforts at colonisation in the Americas met with mixed success. An attempt to establish a colony in <a href="/wiki/British_Guiana" title="British Guiana">Guiana</a> in 1604 lasted only two years and failed in its main objective to find gold deposits.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> Colonies on the Caribbean islands of <a href="/wiki/Saint_Lucia" title="Saint Lucia">St Lucia</a> (1605) and <a href="/wiki/Grenada" title="Grenada">Grenada</a> (1609) rapidly folded.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Canny,_p._221_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-Canny,_p._221-30">[30]</a></sup> The first permanent English settlement in the Americas was founded in 1607 in <a href="/wiki/Jamestown,_Virginia" title="Jamestown, Virginia">Jamestown</a> by Captain <a href="/wiki/John_Smith_(explorer)" title="John Smith (explorer)">John Smith</a>, and managed by the <a href="/wiki/London_Company" title="London Company">Virginia Company</a>; the Crown took direct control of the venture in 1624, thereby founding the <a href="/wiki/Colony_of_Virginia" title="Colony of Virginia">Colony of Virginia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bermuda" title="Bermuda">Bermuda</a> was settled and claimed by England as a result of the 1609 shipwreck of the Virginia Company's <a href="/wiki/Sea_Venture" title="Sea Venture">flagship</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> while <a href="/wiki/London_and_Bristol_Company" title="London and Bristol Company">attempts to settle Newfoundland</a> were largely unsuccessful.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> In 1620, <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_Colony" title="Plymouth Colony">Plymouth</a> was founded as a haven by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Puritan" title="Puritan">Puritan</a> religious separatists, later known as the <a href="/wiki/Pilgrims_(Plymouth_Colony)" title="Pilgrims (Plymouth Colony)">Pilgrims</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> Fleeing from <a href="/wiki/Religious_persecution" title="Religious persecution">religious persecution</a> would become the motive for many English would-be colonists to risk the arduous <a href="/wiki/Transatlantic_crossing" title="Transatlantic crossing">trans-Atlantic voyage</a>: <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Maryland" title="Province of Maryland">Maryland</a> was established by <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church_in_England_and_Wales" title="Catholic Church in England and Wales">English Roman Catholics</a> (1634), <a href="/wiki/Colony_of_Rhode_Island_and_Providence_Plantations" title="Colony of Rhode Island and Providence Plantations">Rhode Island</a> (1636) as a colony <a href="/wiki/Religious_tolerance" title="Religious tolerance">tolerant of all religions</a> and Connecticut (1639) for <a href="/wiki/Congregational_church" title="Congregational church">Congregationalists</a>. England's North American holdings were further expanded by the annexation of the Dutch colony of <a href="/wiki/New_Netherland" title="New Netherland">New Netherland</a> in 1664, following the capture of <a href="/wiki/New_Amsterdam" title="New Amsterdam">New Amsterdam</a>, which was renamed <a href="/wiki/New_York_(state)" title="New York (state)">New York</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> Although less financially successful than colonies in the Caribbean, these territories had large areas of good agricultural land and attracted far greater numbers of English emigrants, who preferred their temperate climates.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2004b72–73_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2004b72–73-36">[36]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/British_West_Indies" title="British West Indies">British West Indies</a> initially provided England's most important and lucrative colonies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> Settlements were successfully established in <a href="/wiki/Saint_Kitts" title="Saint Kitts">St. Kitts</a> (1624), <a href="/wiki/Barbados" title="Barbados">Barbados</a> (1627) and <a href="/wiki/Nevis" title="Nevis">Nevis</a> (1628),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Canny,_p._221_30-1"><a href="#cite_note-Canny,_p._221-30">[30]</a></sup> but struggled until the "Sugar Revolution" transformed the Caribbean economy in the mid-17th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_Watson_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_Watson-38">[38]</a></sup> Large <a href="/wiki/Sugar_plantations_in_the_Caribbean" title="Sugar plantations in the Caribbean">sugarcane plantations</a> were first established in the 1640s on Barbados, with assistance from Dutch merchants and <a href="/wiki/Sephardi_Jews" title="Sephardi Jews">Sephardic Jews</a> fleeing <a href="/wiki/Colonial_Brazil" title="Colonial Brazil">Portuguese Brazil</a>. At first, sugar was grown primarily using white <a href="/wiki/Indentured_servitude_in_British_America" title="Indentured servitude in British America">indentured labour</a>, but rising costs soon led English traders to embrace the use of imported African slaves.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHigman2000224_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHigman2000224-39">[39]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERichardson202224_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERichardson202224-40">[40]</a></sup> The enormous wealth generated by slave-produced sugar made Barbados the most successful colony in the Americas,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHigman2000224–225_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHigman2000224–225-41">[41]</a></sup> and one of the most densely populated places in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_Watson_38-1"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_Watson-38">[38]</a></sup> This boom led to the spread of sugar cultivation across the Caribbean, financed the development of non-plantation colonies in North America, and accelerated the growth of the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_slave_trade" title="Atlantic slave trade">Atlantic slave trade</a>, particularly the <a href="/wiki/Triangular_trade" title="Triangular trade">triangular trade</a> of slaves, sugar and provisions between Africa, the West Indies and Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHigman2000225–226_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHigman2000225–226-42">[42]</a></sup>
</p><p>To ensure that the increasingly healthy profits of colonial trade remained in English hands, Parliament <a href="/wiki/Navigation_Acts" title="Navigation Acts">decreed</a> in 1651 that only English ships would be able to ply their trade in English colonies. This led to hostilities with the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Republic" title="Dutch Republic">United Dutch Provinces</a>—a series of <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Dutch_Wars" title="Anglo-Dutch Wars">Anglo-Dutch Wars</a>—which would eventually strengthen England's position in the Americas at the expense of the Dutch.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> In 1655, England annexed the island of <a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">Jamaica</a> from the Spanish, and in 1666 succeeded in colonising the <a href="/wiki/The_Bahamas" title="The Bahamas">Bahamas</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup>
In 1670, <a href="/wiki/Charles_II_of_England" title="Charles II of England">Charles II</a> incorporated by royal charter the <a href="/wiki/Hudson%27s_Bay_Company" title="Hudson's Bay Company">Hudson's Bay Company</a> (HBC), granting it a monopoly on the <a href="/wiki/North_American_fur_trade" title="North American fur trade">fur trade</a> in the area known as <a href="/wiki/Rupert%27s_Land" title="Rupert's Land">Rupert's Land</a>, which would later form a large proportion of the <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Dominion of Canada</a>. Forts and trading posts established by the HBC were frequently the subject of attacks by the French, who had established their own fur trading colony in adjacent <a href="/wiki/New_France" title="New France">New France</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-buckner25_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-buckner25-45">[45]</a></sup>
</p><p>Two years later, the <a href="/wiki/Royal_African_Company" title="Royal African Company">Royal African Company</a> was granted a monopoly on the supply of slaves to the British colonies in the Caribbean.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> The company would transport more slaves across the Atlantic than any other, and significantly grew England's share of the trade, from 33 per cent in 1673 to 74 per cent in 1683.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> The removal of this monopoly between 1688 and 1712 allowed independent British slave traders to thrive, leading to a rapid escalation in the number of slaves transported.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> British ships carried a third of all slaves shipped across the Atlantic—approximately 3.5 million Africans<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2004b62_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2004b62-49">[49]</a></sup>—and dominated global slave trading in the 25 years preceding its abolition by Parliament in 1807 (see <a href="#Abolition_of_slavery">§ Abolition of slavery</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERichardson202223_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERichardson202223-50">[50]</a></sup> To facilitate the shipment of slaves, forts were established on the coast of West Africa, such as <a href="/wiki/Kunta_Kinteh_Island" title="Kunta Kinteh Island">James Island</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jamestown,_Ghana" title="Jamestown, Ghana">Accra</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bunce_Island" title="Bunce Island">Bunce Island</a>. In the British Caribbean, the percentage of the population of African descent rose from 25 per cent in 1650 to around 80 per cent in 1780, and in the Thirteen Colonies from 10 per cent to 40 per cent over the same period (the majority in the southern colonies).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> The transatlantic slave trade played a pervasive role in British economic life, and became a major economic mainstay for western port cities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> Ships registered in <a href="/wiki/Bristol" title="Bristol">Bristol</a>, <a href="/wiki/Liverpool" title="Liverpool">Liverpool</a> and <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a> were responsible for the bulk of British slave trading.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENellis201330_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENellis201330-53">[53]</a></sup> For the transported, harsh and unhygienic conditions on the slaving ships and poor diets meant that the average <a href="/wiki/Mortality_rate" title="Mortality rate">mortality rate</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Passage" title="Middle Passage">Middle Passage</a> was one in seven.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rivalry_with_other_European_empires">Rivalry with other European empires</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/East_India_Company" title="East India Company">East India Company</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Fort_St._George,_Chennai.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="826" data-file-width="1280" decoding="async" height="142" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Fort_St._George%2C_Chennai.jpg/220px-Fort_St._George%2C_Chennai.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Fort_St._George%2C_Chennai.jpg/330px-Fort_St._George%2C_Chennai.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Fort_St._George%2C_Chennai.jpg/440px-Fort_St._George%2C_Chennai.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Fort_St._George,_Chennai.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Fort_St._George,_India" title="Fort St. George, India">Fort St. George</a> was founded at <a href="/wiki/Chennai" title="Chennai">Madras</a> in 1639.</div></div></div>
<p>At the end of the 16th century, England and the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Empire" title="Dutch Empire">Dutch Empire</a> began to challenge the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">Portuguese Empire</a>'s monopoly of trade with Asia, forming private joint-stock companies to finance the voyages—the English, later British, East India Company and the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_India_Company" title="Dutch East India Company">Dutch East India Company</a>, chartered in 1600 and 1602 respectively. The primary aim of these companies was to tap into the lucrative <a href="/wiki/Spice_trade" title="Spice trade">spice trade</a>, an effort focused mainly on two regions: the <a href="/wiki/Malay_Archipelago" title="Malay Archipelago">East Indies archipelago</a>, and an important hub in the trade network, India. There, they competed for trade supremacy with Portugal and with each other.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> Although England eclipsed the Netherlands as a colonial power, in the short term the Netherlands' more advanced financial system<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2004b19_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2004b19-56">[56]</a></sup> and the three <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Dutch_Wars" title="Anglo-Dutch Wars">Anglo-Dutch Wars</a> of the 17th century left it with a stronger position in Asia. Hostilities ceased after the <a href="/wiki/Glorious_Revolution" title="Glorious Revolution">Glorious Revolution</a> of 1688 when the Dutch <a href="/wiki/William_III_of_England" title="William III of England">William of Orange</a> ascended the English throne, bringing peace between the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Republic" title="Dutch Republic">Dutch Republic</a> and England. A deal between the two nations left the <a href="/wiki/Spice_trade" title="Spice trade">spice trade</a> of the <a href="/wiki/East_Indies" title="East Indies">East Indies</a> archipelago to the Netherlands and the <a href="/wiki/Textile_industry_in_India" title="Textile industry in India">textiles industry of India</a> to England, but textiles soon overtook spices in terms of profitability.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2004b19_56-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2004b19-56">[56]</a></sup>
</p><p>Peace between England and the Netherlands in 1688 meant the two countries entered the <a href="/wiki/Nine_Years%27_War" title="Nine Years' War">Nine Years' War</a> as allies, but the conflict—waged in Europe and overseas between France, Spain and the Anglo-Dutch alliance—left the English a stronger colonial power than the Dutch, who were forced to devote a larger proportion of their <a href="/wiki/Military_budget" title="Military budget">military budget</a> to the costly land war in Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> The death of <a href="/wiki/Charles_II_of_Spain" title="Charles II of Spain">Charles II of Spain</a> in 1700 and his bequeathal of Spain and its colonial empire to <a href="/wiki/Philip_V_of_Spain" title="Philip V of Spain">Philip V of Spain</a>, a grandson of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Louis_XIV_of_France" title="Louis XIV of France">King of France</a>, raised the prospect of the unification of France, Spain and their respective colonies, an unacceptable state of affairs for England and the other powers of Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-shennan11_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-shennan11-58">[58]</a></sup> In 1701, England, Portugal and the Netherlands sided with the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a> against Spain and France in the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Spanish_Succession" title="War of the Spanish Succession">War of the Spanish Succession</a>, which lasted for thirteen years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-shennan11_58-1"><a href="#cite_note-shennan11-58">[58]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Scottish_attempt_to_expand_overseas">Scottish attempt to expand overseas</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Scottish_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="Scottish colonization of the Americas">Scottish colonization of the Americas</a></div>
<p>In 1695, the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Scotland" title="Parliament of Scotland">Parliament of Scotland</a> granted a charter to the <a href="/wiki/Company_of_Scotland" title="Company of Scotland">Company of Scotland</a>, which established a settlement in 1698 on the <a href="/wiki/Isthmus_of_Panama" title="Isthmus of Panama">Isthmus of Panama</a>. Besieged by neighbouring Spanish colonists of <a href="/wiki/New_Kingdom_of_Granada" title="New Kingdom of Granada">New Granada</a>, and affected by <a href="/wiki/Malaria" title="Malaria">malaria</a>, the colony was abandoned two years later. The <a href="/wiki/Darien_scheme" title="Darien scheme">Darien scheme</a> was a financial disaster for Scotland—a quarter of Scottish capital<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> was lost in the enterprise—and ended Scottish hopes of establishing its own overseas empire. The episode had major political consequences, helping to persuade the government of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Scotland" title="Kingdom of Scotland">Kingdom of Scotland</a> of the merits of turning the <a href="/wiki/Personal_union" title="Personal union">personal union</a> with England into a political and economic one under the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Great_Britain" title="Kingdom of Great Britain">Kingdom of Great Britain</a> established by the <a href="/wiki/Acts_of_Union_1707" title="Acts of Union 1707">Acts of Union 1707</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span id=".22First.22_British_Empire_.281707.E2.80.931783.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id='"First"_British_Empire_(1707–1783)'>"First" British Empire (1707–1783)</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Clive.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1870" data-file-width="2400" decoding="async" height="171" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Clive.jpg/220px-Clive.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Clive.jpg/330px-Clive.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Clive.jpg/440px-Clive.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Clive.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Robert_Clive" title="Robert Clive">Robert Clive</a>'s victory at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Plassey" title="Battle of Plassey">Battle of Plassey</a> established the <a href="/wiki/East_India_Company" title="East India Company">East India Company</a> as a military as well as a commercial power.</div></div></div>
<p>The 18th century saw the <a href="/wiki/Acts_of_Union_1707" title="Acts of Union 1707">newly united</a> Great Britain rise to be the world's dominant colonial power, with France becoming its main rival on the imperial stage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> Great Britain, Portugal, the Netherlands, and the Holy Roman Empire continued the War of the Spanish Succession, which lasted until 1714 and was concluded by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Utrecht" title="Treaty of Utrecht">Treaty of Utrecht</a>. <a href="/wiki/Philip_V_of_Spain" title="Philip V of Spain">Philip V of Spain</a> renounced his and his descendants' claim to the French throne, and Spain lost its empire in Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-shennan11_58-2"><a href="#cite_note-shennan11-58">[58]</a></sup> The British Empire was territorially enlarged: from France, Britain gained <a href="/wiki/Newfoundland_Colony" title="Newfoundland Colony">Newfoundland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Acadia" title="Acadia">Acadia</a>, and from Spain <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar" title="Gibraltar">Gibraltar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Menorca" title="Menorca">Menorca</a>. Gibraltar became a <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Squadron" title="Gibraltar Squadron">critical naval base</a> and allowed Britain to control the <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Gibraltar" title="Strait of Gibraltar">Atlantic entry and exit point</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">Mediterranean</a>. Spain ceded the rights to the lucrative <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asiento" title="Asiento">asiento</a></i> (permission to sell African slaves in <a href="/wiki/Spanish_America" title="Spanish America">Spanish America</a>) to Britain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> With the outbreak of the Anglo-Spanish <a href="/wiki/War_of_Jenkins%27_Ear" title="War of Jenkins' Ear">War of Jenkins' Ear</a> in 1739, Spanish privateers attacked British merchant shipping along the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Triangle_Trade" title="Triangle Trade">Triangle Trade</a> routes. In 1746, the Spanish and British began peace talks, with the King of Spain agreeing to stop all attacks on British shipping; however, in the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Madrid_(5_October_1750)" title="Treaty of Madrid (5 October 1750)">Treaty of Madrid</a> Britain lost its slave-trading rights in <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the East Indies, British and Dutch merchants continued to compete in spices and textiles. With textiles becoming the larger trade, by 1720, in terms of sales, the British company had overtaken the Dutch.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2004b19_56-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2004b19-56">[56]</a></sup> During the middle decades of the 18th century, there were <a href="/wiki/Carnatic_Wars" title="Carnatic Wars">several outbreaks of military conflict</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Indian_subcontinent" title="Indian subcontinent">Indian subcontinent</a>, as the English East India Company and its <a href="/wiki/French_East_India_Company" title="French East India Company">French counterpart</a>, struggled alongside local rulers to fill the vacuum that had been left by the decline of the <a href="/wiki/Mughal_Empire" title="Mughal Empire">Mughal Empire</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Plassey" title="Battle of Plassey">Battle of Plassey</a> in 1757, in which the British defeated the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nawab_of_Bengal" title="Nawab of Bengal">Nawab of Bengal</a> and his French allies, left the British East India Company in control of <a href="/wiki/Bengal" title="Bengal">Bengal</a> and as the major military and political power in India.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> France was left control of its <a href="/wiki/French_India" title="French India">enclaves</a> but with military restrictions and an obligation to support British <a href="/wiki/Client_state" title="Client state">client states</a>, ending French hopes of controlling India.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> In the following decades the British East India Company gradually increased the size of the territories under its control, either ruling directly or via local rulers under the threat of force from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Presidency_Armies" title="Presidency Armies">Presidency Armies</a>, the vast majority of which was composed of Indian <a href="/wiki/Sepoy" title="Sepoy">sepoys</a>, led by British officers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> The British and French struggles in India became but one theatre of the global <a href="/wiki/Seven_Years%27_War" title="Seven Years' War">Seven Years' War</a> (1756–1763) involving France, Britain, and the other major European powers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-buckner25_45-1"><a href="#cite_note-buckner25-45">[45]</a></sup>
</p><p>The signing of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1763)" title="Treaty of Paris (1763)">Treaty of Paris of 1763</a> had important consequences for the future of the British Empire. In North America, France's future as a colonial power effectively ended with the recognition of British claims to Rupert's Land,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-buckner25_45-2"><a href="#cite_note-buckner25-45">[45]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Conquest_of_New_France_(1758%E2%80%931760)" title="Conquest of New France (1758–1760)">ceding of New France to Britain</a> (leaving a sizeable <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French_Canadian" title="French Canadian">French-speaking population</a> under British control) and <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_(New_France)" title="Louisiana (New France)">Louisiana</a> to Spain. Spain ceded Florida to Britain. Along with its victory over France in India, the Seven Years' War therefore left Britain as the world's most powerful <a href="/wiki/Maritime_power" title="Maritime power">maritime power</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-refpagden1_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-refpagden1-67">[67]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Loss_of_the_Thirteen_American_Colonies">Loss of the Thirteen American Colonies</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/American_Revolution" title="American Revolution">American Revolution</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, <a href="/wiki/Decolonization_of_the_Americas" title="Decolonization of the Americas">Decolonization of the Americas</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_North_America" title="British North America">British North America</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_Canada_(1763%E2%80%931867)" title="History of Canada (1763–1867)">History of Canada (1763–1867)</a>, and <a href="/wiki/War_of_1812" title="War of 1812">War of 1812</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:British_America.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="329" data-file-width="383" decoding="async" height="223" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/British_America.png/260px-British_America.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/75/British_America.png 1.5x" width="260"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:British_America.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>British territories in the Americas, 1763–1776, extending much further than the <a href="/wiki/Thirteen_Colonies" title="Thirteen Colonies">Thirteen Colonies</a> on the Atlantic coast</div></div></div>
<p>During the 1760s and early 1770s, relations between the Thirteen Colonies and Britain became increasingly strained, primarily because of resentment of the British Parliament's attempts to govern and tax American colonists without their consent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2004b84_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2004b84-68">[68]</a></sup> This was summarised at the time by the slogan "<a href="/wiki/No_taxation_without_representation" title="No taxation without representation">No taxation without representation</a>", a perceived violation of the guaranteed <a href="/wiki/Rights_of_Englishmen" title="Rights of Englishmen">Rights of Englishmen</a>. The <a href="/wiki/American_Revolution" title="American Revolution">American Revolution</a> began with a rejection of Parliamentary authority and moves towards self-government. In response, Britain sent troops to reimpose direct rule, leading to the outbreak of war in 1775. The following year, in 1776, the <a href="/wiki/Second_Continental_Congress" title="Second Continental Congress">Second Continental Congress</a> issued the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Declaration_of_Independence" title="United States Declaration of Independence">Declaration of Independence</a> proclaiming the colonies' sovereignty from the British Empire as the new <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_of_America" title="United States of America">United States of America</a>. The entry of <a href="/wiki/France_in_the_American_Revolutionary_War" title="France in the American Revolutionary War">French</a> and <a href="/wiki/Spain_and_the_American_Revolutionary_War" title="Spain and the American Revolutionary War">Spanish forces</a> into the war tipped the military balance in the Americans' favour and after a decisive defeat at <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Yorktown" title="Siege of Yorktown">Yorktown</a> in 1781, Britain began negotiating peace terms. American independence was acknowledged at the <a href="/wiki/Peace_of_Paris_(1783)" title="Peace of Paris (1783)">Peace of Paris</a> in 1783.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup>
</p><p>The loss of such a large portion of <a href="/wiki/British_America" title="British America">British America</a>, at the time Britain's most populous overseas possession, is seen by some historians as the event defining the transition between the "first" and "second" empires,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> in which Britain shifted its attention away from the Americas to Asia, the Pacific and later Africa. <a href="/wiki/Adam_Smith" title="Adam Smith">Adam Smith</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/The_Wealth_of_Nations" title="The Wealth of Nations">Wealth of Nations</a></i>, published in 1776, had argued that colonies were redundant, and that <a href="/wiki/Free_trade" title="Free trade">free trade</a> should replace the old <a href="/wiki/Mercantilism" title="Mercantilism">mercantilist</a> policies that had characterised the first period of colonial expansion, dating back to the <a href="/wiki/Protectionism" title="Protectionism">protectionism</a> of Spain and Portugal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-refpagden1_67-1"><a href="#cite_note-refpagden1-67">[67]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> The growth of trade between the newly independent <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> and Britain after 1783 seemed to confirm Smith's view that political control was not necessary for economic success.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup>
</p><p>The war to the south influenced British policy in Canada, where between 40,000 and 100,000<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> defeated <a href="/wiki/Loyalist_(American_Revolution)" title="Loyalist (American Revolution)">Loyalists</a> had migrated from the new United States following independence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> The 14,000 Loyalists who went to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saint_John_River_(New_Brunswick)" title="Saint John River (New Brunswick)">Saint John</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saint_Croix_River_(Maine_%E2%80%93_New_Brunswick)" title="Saint Croix River (Maine – New Brunswick)">Saint Croix river</a> valleys, then part of <a href="/wiki/Nova_Scotia" title="Nova Scotia">Nova Scotia</a>, felt too far removed from the provincial government in <a href="/wiki/Halifax,_Nova_Scotia" title="Halifax, Nova Scotia">Halifax</a>, so London split off <a href="/wiki/New_Brunswick" title="New Brunswick">New Brunswick</a> as a separate colony in 1784.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Constitutional_Act_of_1791" title="Constitutional Act of 1791">Constitutional Act of 1791</a> created the provinces of <a href="/wiki/Upper_Canada" title="Upper Canada">Upper Canada</a> (mainly <a href="/wiki/English_Canada" title="English Canada">English speaking</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Lower_Canada" title="Lower Canada">Lower Canada</a> (mainly <a href="/wiki/French_Canadians" title="French Canadians">French-speaking</a>) to defuse tensions between the French and British communities, and implemented governmental systems similar to those employed in Britain, with the intention of asserting imperial authority and not allowing the sort of popular control of government that was perceived to have led to the American Revolution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup>
</p><p>Tensions between Britain and the United States escalated again during the <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars" title="Napoleonic Wars">Napoleonic Wars</a>, as Britain tried to cut off American trade with France and boarded American ships to <a href="/wiki/Impressment" title="Impressment">impress</a> men into the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a>. The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Congress" title="United States Congress">United States Congress</a> declared war, the <a href="/wiki/War_of_1812" title="War of 1812">War of 1812</a>, and invaded Canadian territory. In response, Britain invaded the US, but the pre-war boundaries were reaffirmed by the 1814 <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Ghent" title="Treaty of Ghent">Treaty of Ghent</a>, ensuring Canada's future would be separate from that of the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span id="Rise_of_the_.22Second.22_British_Empire_.281783.E2.80.931815.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id='Rise_of_the_"Second"_British_Empire_(1783–1815)'>Rise of the "Second" British Empire (1783–1815)</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Exploration_of_the_Pacific">Exploration of the Pacific</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Australia_(1788%E2%80%931850)" title="History of Australia (1788–1850)">History of Australia (1788–1850)</a> and <a href="/wiki/History_of_New_Zealand" title="History of New Zealand">History of New Zealand</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Captainjamescookportrait.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="7692" data-file-width="6131" decoding="async" height="213" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Captainjamescookportrait.jpg/170px-Captainjamescookportrait.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Captainjamescookportrait.jpg/255px-Captainjamescookportrait.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Captainjamescookportrait.jpg/340px-Captainjamescookportrait.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Captainjamescookportrait.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/James_Cook" title="James Cook">James Cook</a>'s mission was to find the alleged southern continent <i><a href="/wiki/Terra_Australis" title="Terra Australis">Terra Australis</a></i>.</div></div></div>
<p>Since 1718, <a href="/wiki/Penal_transportation" title="Penal transportation">transportation</a> to the American colonies had been a penalty for various offences in Britain, with approximately one thousand convicts transported per year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> Forced to find an alternative location after the loss of the Thirteen Colonies in 1783, the British government turned to <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/New_Holland_(Australia)" title="New Holland (Australia)">coast of Australia</a> had been discovered for Europeans by the Dutch <a href="/wiki/Janszoon_voyage_of_1605%E2%80%9306" title="Janszoon voyage of 1605–06">in 1606</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-82">[82]</a></sup> but there was no attempt to colonise it. In 1770 <a href="/wiki/James_Cook" title="James Cook">James Cook</a> charted the eastern coast while on a scientific <a href="/wiki/First_voyage_of_James_Cook" title="First voyage of James Cook">voyage</a>, claimed the continent for Britain, and named it <a href="/wiki/Colony_of_New_South_Wales" title="Colony of New South Wales">New South Wales</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> In 1778, <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Banks" title="Joseph Banks">Joseph Banks</a>, Cook's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Botanist" title="Botanist">botanist</a> on the voyage, presented evidence to the government on the suitability of <a href="/wiki/Botany_Bay" title="Botany Bay">Botany Bay</a> for the establishment of a <a href="/wiki/Penal_colony" title="Penal colony">penal settlement</a>, and in 1787 the first shipment of <a href="/wiki/Convicts_in_Australia" title="Convicts in Australia">convicts</a> set sail, arriving in 1788.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> Unusually, Australia was claimed through proclamation. <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_Australians" title="Indigenous Australians">Indigenous Australians</a> were considered too uncivilised to require treaties,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> and colonisation brought disease and violence that together with the deliberate dispossession of land and culture were devastating to these peoples.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> Britain continued to transport convicts to New South Wales until 1840, to <a href="/wiki/Colony_of_Tasmania" title="Colony of Tasmania">Tasmania</a> until 1853 and to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Colony_of_Western_Australia" title="Colony of Western Australia">Western Australia</a> until 1868.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> The Australian colonies became profitable exporters of wool and gold,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> mainly because of the <a href="/wiki/Victorian_gold_rush" title="Victorian gold rush">Victorian gold rush</a>, making its capital <a href="/wiki/Melbourne" title="Melbourne">Melbourne</a> for a time the richest city in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup>
</p><p>During his voyage, Cook visited <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a>, known to Europeans due to the 1642 voyage of Dutch explorer <a href="/wiki/Abel_Tasman" title="Abel Tasman">Abel Tasman</a>, and claimed both the <a href="/wiki/North_Island" title="North Island">North</a> and the <a href="/wiki/South_Island" title="South Island">South</a> islands for the British crown in 1769 and 1770 respectively. Initially, interaction between the indigenous <a href="/wiki/M%C4%81ori_people" title="Māori people">Māori</a> population and European <a href="/wiki/P%C4%81keh%C4%81_settlers" title="Pākehā settlers">Pākehā settlers</a> was limited to the trading of goods. European settlement increased through the early decades of the 19th century, with numerous trading stations established, especially in the North. In 1839, the <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand_Company" title="New Zealand Company">New Zealand Company</a> announced plans to buy large tracts of land and establish colonies in New Zealand. On 6 February 1840, Captain <a href="/wiki/William_Hobson" title="William Hobson">William Hobson</a> and around 40 Maori chiefs signed the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Waitangi" title="Treaty of Waitangi">Treaty of Waitangi</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> This treaty is considered to be New Zealand's founding document,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> but differing interpretations of the <a href="/wiki/M%C4%81ori_language" title="Māori language">Maori</a> and <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> versions of the text<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> have meant that it continues to be a source of dispute.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup>
</p><p>The British also expanded their mercantile interests in the North Pacific. Spain and Britain had become rivals in the area, culminating in the <a href="/wiki/Nootka_Crisis" title="Nootka Crisis">Nootka Crisis</a> in 1789. Both sides mobilised for war, but when France refused to support Spain it was forced to back down, leading to the <a href="/wiki/Nootka_Convention" title="Nootka Convention">Nootka Convention</a>. The outcome was a humiliation for Spain, which practically renounced all sovereignty on the North Pacific coast.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> This opened the way to British expansion in the area, and a number of expeditions took place; firstly a <a href="/wiki/Vancouver_Expedition" title="Vancouver Expedition">naval expedition</a> led by <a href="/wiki/George_Vancouver" title="George Vancouver">George Vancouver</a> which explored the inlets around the Pacific North West, particularly around <a href="/wiki/Vancouver_Island" title="Vancouver Island">Vancouver Island</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pethick0_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-pethick0-97">[97]</a></sup> On land, expeditions sought to discover a river route to the Pacific for the extension of the <a href="/wiki/North_American_fur_trade" title="North American fur trade">North American fur trade</a>. <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Mackenzie_(explorer)" title="Alexander Mackenzie (explorer)">Alexander Mackenzie</a> of the <a href="/wiki/North_West_Company" title="North West Company">North West Company</a> led the first, starting out in 1792, and a year a later he became the first European to reach the Pacific overland north of the <a href="/wiki/Rio_Grande" title="Rio Grande">Rio Grande</a>, reaching the ocean near present-day <a href="/wiki/Bella_Coola,_British_Columbia" title="Bella Coola, British Columbia">Bella Coola</a>. This preceded the <a href="/wiki/Lewis_and_Clark_Expedition" title="Lewis and Clark Expedition">Lewis and Clark Expedition</a> by twelve years. Shortly thereafter, Mackenzie's companion, <a href="/wiki/John_Finlay_(fur_trader)" title="John Finlay (fur trader)">John Finlay</a>, founded the first permanent European settlement in <a href="/wiki/British_Columbia" title="British Columbia">British Columbia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fort_St._John,_British_Columbia" title="Fort St. John, British Columbia">Fort St. John</a>. The North West Company sought further exploration and backed expeditions by <a href="/wiki/David_Thompson_(explorer)" title="David Thompson (explorer)">David Thompson</a>, starting in 1797, and later by <a href="/wiki/Simon_Fraser_(explorer)" title="Simon Fraser (explorer)">Simon Fraser</a>. These pushed into the wilderness territories of the <a href="/wiki/Rocky_Mountains" title="Rocky Mountains">Rocky Mountains</a> and <a href="/wiki/Interior_Plateau" title="Interior Plateau">Interior Plateau</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Georgia" title="Strait of Georgia">Strait of Georgia</a> on the Pacific Coast, expanding <a href="/wiki/British_North_America" title="British North America">British North America</a> westward.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-innes_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-innes-98">[98]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wars_with_France">Wars with France</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/French_Revolutionary_and_Napoleonic_Wars" title="French Revolutionary and Napoleonic Wars">French Revolutionary and Napoleonic Wars</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Waterloo_1815.PNG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="846" data-file-width="1854" decoding="async" height="151" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Battle_of_Waterloo_1815.PNG/330px-Battle_of_Waterloo_1815.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Battle_of_Waterloo_1815.PNG/495px-Battle_of_Waterloo_1815.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Battle_of_Waterloo_1815.PNG/660px-Battle_of_Waterloo_1815.PNG 2x" width="330"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Waterloo_1815.PNG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Waterloo" title="Battle of Waterloo">Battle of Waterloo</a> in 1815 ended in the defeat of <a href="/wiki/Napoleon" title="Napoleon">Napoleon</a> and marked the beginning of <i><a href="/wiki/Pax_Britannica" title="Pax Britannica">Pax Britannica</a></i>.</div></div></div>
<p>Britain was challenged again by France under Napoleon, in a struggle that, unlike previous wars, represented a contest of ideologies between the two nations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> It was not only Britain's position on the world stage that was at risk: Napoleon threatened to invade Britain itself, just as his armies had overrun many countries of <a href="/wiki/Continental_Europe" title="Continental Europe">continental Europe</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Napoleonic Wars were therefore ones in which Britain invested large amounts of capital and resources to win. French ports were blockaded by the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a>, which won a decisive victory over a <a href="/wiki/French_Imperial_Navy" title="French Imperial Navy">French Imperial Navy</a>-<a href="/wiki/Spanish_Navy" title="Spanish Navy">Spanish Navy</a> fleet at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Trafalgar" title="Battle of Trafalgar">Battle of Trafalgar</a> in 1805. Overseas colonies were attacked and occupied, including those of the Netherlands, which was annexed by Napoleon in 1810. France was finally defeated by a coalition of European armies in 1815.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> Britain was again the beneficiary of peace treaties: France ceded the <a href="/wiki/United_States_of_the_Ionian_Islands" title="United States of the Ionian Islands">Ionian Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malta_Protectorate" title="Malta Protectorate">Malta</a> (which it had occupied in 1798), <a href="/wiki/British_Mauritius" title="British Mauritius">Mauritius</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St_Lucia" title="St Lucia">St Lucia</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Seychelles" title="Seychelles">Seychelles</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tobago" title="Tobago">Tobago</a>; Spain ceded <a href="/wiki/Trinidad" title="Trinidad">Trinidad</a>; the Netherlands ceded <a href="/wiki/Guyana" title="Guyana">Guyana</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_Ceylon" title="British Ceylon">Ceylon</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Cape_Colony" title="Cape Colony">Cape Colony</a>, while the Danish ceded <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_Administration_of_Heligoland" title="British Administration of Heligoland">Heligoland</a>. Britain returned <a href="/wiki/Guadeloupe" title="Guadeloupe">Guadeloupe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Martinique" title="Martinique">Martinique</a>, <a href="/wiki/French_Guiana" title="French Guiana">French Guiana</a>, and <a href="/wiki/R%C3%A9union" title="Réunion">Réunion</a> to France; <a href="/wiki/Menorca" title="Menorca">Menorca</a> to Spain; <a href="/wiki/Danish_West_Indies" title="Danish West Indies">Danish West Indies</a> to Denmark and <a href="/wiki/Java" title="Java">Java</a> and <a href="/wiki/Suriname" title="Suriname">Suriname</a> to the Netherlands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-refjames165_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-refjames165-102">[102]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Abolition_of_slavery">Abolition of slavery</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Abolitionism_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Abolitionism in the United Kingdom">Abolitionism in the United Kingdom</a></div>
<p>With the advent of the <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">Industrial Revolution</a>, goods produced by slavery became less important to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_economy" title="British economy">British economy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> Added to this was the cost of suppressing regular <a href="/wiki/Slave_rebellion" title="Slave rebellion">slave rebellions</a>. With support from the British <a href="/wiki/Abolitionism_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Abolitionism in the United Kingdom">abolitionist</a> movement, <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Parliament of the United Kingdom">Parliament</a> enacted the <a href="/wiki/Slave_Trade_Act_1807" title="Slave Trade Act 1807">Slave Trade Act</a> in 1807, which abolished the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slave_trade" title="Slave trade">slave trade</a> in the empire. In 1808, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sierra_Leone_Colony" title="Sierra Leone Colony">Sierra Leone Colony</a> was designated an official British colony for freed slaves.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> Parliamentary reform in 1832 saw the influence of the <a href="/wiki/West_India_Committee" title="West India Committee">West India Committee</a> decline. The <a href="/wiki/Slavery_Abolition_Act_1833" title="Slavery Abolition Act 1833">Slavery Abolition Act</a>, passed the following year, abolished slavery in the British Empire on 1 August 1834, finally bringing the Empire into line with the law in the UK (with the exception of the territories administered by the East India Company and Ceylon, where slavery was ended in 1844). Under the Act, slaves were granted full emancipation after a period of four to six years of "apprenticeship".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> Facing further opposition from abolitionists, the apprenticeship system was abolished in 1838.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> The British government compensated slave-owners.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Manning_108-0"><a href="#cite_note-Manning-108">[108]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span id="Britain.27s_imperial_century_.281815.E2.80.931914.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Britain's_imperial_century_(1815–1914)">Britain's imperial century (1815–1914)</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_British_diplomatic_history#1815–1860" title="Timeline of British diplomatic history">Timeline of British diplomatic history § 1815–1860</a>, <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">Industrial Revolution</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Victorian_era" title="Victorian era">Victorian era</a></div>
<p>Between 1815 and 1914, a period referred to as Britain's "imperial century" by some historians,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> around 10 million sq mi (26 million km<sup>2</sup>) of territory and roughly 400 million people were added to the British Empire.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> Victory over Napoleon left Britain without any serious international rival, other than <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Great_Game" title="The Great Game">Russia in Central Asia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-#refOHBEv3|Porter,_p._401_112-0"><a href="#cite_note-#refOHBEv3|Porter,_p._401-112">[112]</a></sup> Unchallenged at sea, Britain adopted the role of global policeman, a state of affairs later known as the <i><a href="/wiki/Pax_Britannica" title="Pax Britannica">Pax Britannica</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-113">[113]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> and a foreign policy of "<a href="/wiki/Splendid_isolation" title="Splendid isolation">splendid isolation</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> Alongside the formal control it exerted over its own colonies, Britain's dominant position in world trade meant that it effectively controlled the economies of many countries, such as China, Argentina and <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Siam</a>, which has been described by some historians as an "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Informal_Empire" title="Informal Empire">Informal Empire</a>".<sup class="reference"
