id="cite_ref-auto_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-auto-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceC_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceC-7">[7]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Victoria_Disraeli_cartoon.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="393" data-file-width="301" decoding="async" height="222" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Victoria_Disraeli_cartoon.jpg/170px-Victoria_Disraeli_cartoon.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Victoria_Disraeli_cartoon.jpg/255px-Victoria_Disraeli_cartoon.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f2/Victoria_Disraeli_cartoon.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Victoria_Disraeli_cartoon.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An 1876 political cartoon of <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Disraeli" title="Benjamin Disraeli">Benjamin Disraeli</a> (1804–1881) making <a href="/wiki/Queen_Victoria" title="Queen Victoria">Queen Victoria</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Empress_of_India" title="Empress of India">Empress of India</a>. The caption reads "New crowns for old ones!"</div></div></div>
<p>British imperial strength was underpinned by the <a href="/wiki/Steamship" title="Steamship">steamship</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Telegraph" title="Telegraph">telegraph</a>, new technologies invented in the second half of the 19th century, allowing it to control and defend the empire. By 1902, the British Empire was linked together by a network of telegraph cables, called the <a href="/wiki/All_Red_Line" title="All Red Line">All Red Line</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="East_India_Company_rule_and_the_British_Raj_in_India">East India Company rule and the British Raj in India</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Presidencies_and_provinces_of_British_India" title="Presidencies and provinces of British India">Presidencies and provinces of British India</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Company_rule_in_India" title="Company rule in India">Company rule in India</a> and <a href="/wiki/British_Raj" title="British Raj">British Raj</a></div>
<p>The East India Company drove the expansion of the British Empire in Asia. The Company's army had first joined forces with the Royal Navy during the Seven Years' War, and the two continued to co-operate in arenas outside India: the eviction of the French from Egypt (1799),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Java_(1811)" title="Invasion of Java (1811)">capture of Java</a> from the Netherlands (1811), the <a href="/wiki/Penang_Island#History" title="Penang Island">acquisition of Penang Island</a> (1786), <a href="/wiki/Founding_of_modern_Singapore" title="Founding of modern Singapore">Singapore</a> (1819) and <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Dutch_Treaty_of_1824" title="Anglo-Dutch Treaty of 1824">Malacca</a> (1824), and the <a href="/wiki/First_Anglo-Burmese_War" title="First Anglo-Burmese War">defeat of Burma</a> (1826).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-#refOHBEv3|Porter,_p._401_112-1"><a href="#cite_note-#refOHBEv3|Porter,_p._401-112">[112]</a></sup>
</p><p>From its base in India, the Company had been engaged in an increasingly profitable opium export trade to <a href="/wiki/Qing_dynasty" title="Qing dynasty">Qing China</a> since the 1730s. This trade, illegal since it was outlawed by China in 1729, helped reverse the trade imbalances resulting from the British imports of tea, which saw large outflows of silver from Britain to China.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> In 1839, the confiscation by the Chinese authorities at <a href="/wiki/Guangzhou" title="Guangzhou">Canton</a> of 20,000 chests of opium led Britain to attack China in the <a href="/wiki/First_Opium_War" title="First Opium War">First Opium War</a>, and resulted in the seizure by Britain of <a href="/wiki/British_Hong_Kong" title="British Hong Kong">Hong Kong Island</a>, at that time a minor settlement, and other <a href="/wiki/Concessions_in_China" title="Concessions in China">Treaty Ports</a> including <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_International_Settlement" title="Shanghai International Settlement">Shanghai</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup>
</p><p>During the late 18th and early 19th centuries, the British Crown began to assume an increasingly large role in the affairs of the Company. A series of Acts of Parliament were passed, including the <a href="/wiki/Regulating_Act_of_1773" title="Regulating Act of 1773">Regulating Act of 1773</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pitt%27s_India_Act" title="Pitt's India Act">Pitt's India Act</a> of 1784 and the <a href="/wiki/Charter_Act_of_1813" title="Charter Act of 1813">Charter Act of 1813</a> which regulated the Company's affairs and established the sovereignty of the Crown over the territories that it had acquired.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> The Company's eventual end was precipitated by the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Rebellion_of_1857" title="Indian Rebellion of 1857">Indian Rebellion</a> in 1857, a conflict that had begun with the mutiny of sepoys, Indian troops under British officers and discipline.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> The rebellion took six months to suppress, with heavy loss of life on both sides. The following year the British government dissolved the company and assumed direct control over India through the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_India_Act_1858" title="Government of India Act 1858">Government of India Act 1858</a>, establishing the <a href="/wiki/British_Raj" title="British Raj">British Raj</a>, where an appointed <a href="/wiki/Governor-General_of_India" title="Governor-General of India">governor-general</a> administered India and Queen Victoria was crowned the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Empress_of_India" title="Empress of India">Empress of India</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> India became the empire's most valuable possession, "the Jewel in the Crown", and was the most important source of Britain's strength.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brown5_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-Brown5-124">[124]</a></sup>
</p><p>A series of serious crop failures in the late 19th century led to <a href="/wiki/Famine_in_India" title="Famine in India">widespread famines</a> on the subcontinent in which it is estimated that over 15 million people died. The East India Company had failed to implement any coordinated policy to deal with the famines during its period of rule. Later, under direct British rule, commissions were set up after each famine to investigate the causes and implement new policies, which took until the early 1900s to have an effect.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rivalry_with_Russia">Rivalry with Russia</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Great_Game" title="The Great Game">The Great Game</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Relief_of_the_Light_Brigade.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1056" data-file-width="1600" decoding="async" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Relief_of_the_Light_Brigade.png/220px-Relief_of_the_Light_Brigade.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Relief_of_the_Light_Brigade.png/330px-Relief_of_the_Light_Brigade.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Relief_of_the_Light_Brigade.png/440px-Relief_of_the_Light_Brigade.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Relief_of_the_Light_Brigade.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>British cavalry charging against Russian forces at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Balaclava" title="Battle of Balaclava">Balaclava</a> in 1854</div></div></div>
<p>During the 19th century, Britain and the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a> vied to fill the power vacuums that had been left by the declining <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Qajar_dynasty" title="Qajar dynasty">Qajar dynasty</a> and <a href="/wiki/Qing_dynasty" title="Qing dynasty">Qing dynasty</a>. This rivalry in Central Asia came to be known as the "Great Game".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> As far as Britain was concerned, defeats inflicted by Russia on <a href="/wiki/Russo-Persian_War_(1826%E2%80%931828)" title="Russo-Persian War (1826–1828)">Persia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Russo-Turkish_War_(1828%E2%80%931829)" title="Russo-Turkish War (1828–1829)">Turkey</a> demonstrated its imperial ambitions and capabilities and stoked fears in Britain of an overland invasion of India.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> In 1839, Britain moved to pre-empt this by invading <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a>, but the <a href="/wiki/First_Anglo-Afghan_War" title="First Anglo-Afghan War">First Anglo-Afghan War</a> was a disaster for Britain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-refjames182_128-0"><a href="#cite_note-refjames182-128">[128]</a></sup>
</p><p>When Russia invaded the <a href="/wiki/Rumelia" title="Rumelia">Ottoman Balkans</a> in 1853, fears of Russian dominance in the Mediterranean and the Middle East led Britain and France to enter the war in support of the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a> and invade the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crimean_Peninsula" title="Crimean Peninsula">Crimean Peninsula</a> to destroy Russian naval capabilities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-refjames182_128-1"><a href="#cite_note-refjames182-128">[128]</a></sup> The ensuing <a href="/wiki/Crimean_War" title="Crimean War">Crimean War</a> (1854–1856), which involved new techniques of <a href="/wiki/Modern_warfare" title="Modern warfare">modern warfare</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> was the only <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Global_war" title="Global war">global war</a> fought between Britain and another <a href="/wiki/Imperialism" title="Imperialism">imperial power</a> during the <i>Pax Britannica</i> and was a resounding defeat for Russia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-refjames182_128-2"><a href="#cite_note-refjames182-128">[128]</a></sup> The situation remained unresolved in Central Asia for two more decades, with Britain annexing <a href="/wiki/Baluchistan_(Chief_Commissioner%27s_Province)" title="Baluchistan (Chief Commissioner's Province)">Baluchistan</a> in 1876 and Russia annexing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kirghizia" title="Kirghizia">Kirghizia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kazakhstan" title="Kazakhstan">Kazakhstan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Turkmenistan" title="Turkmenistan">Turkmenistan</a>. For a while, it appeared that another war would be inevitable, but the two countries reached an agreement on their respective <a href="/wiki/Sphere_of_influence" title="Sphere of influence">spheres of influence</a> in the region in 1878 and on all outstanding matters in 1907 with the signing of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anglo-Russian_Entente" title="Anglo-Russian Entente">Anglo-Russian Entente</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> The destruction of the <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Russian_Navy" title="Imperial Russian Navy">Imperial Russian Navy</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Japanese_Navy" title="Imperial Japanese Navy">Imperial Japanese Navy</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Port_Arthur" title="Battle of Port Arthur">Battle of Port Arthur</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Russo-Japanese_War" title="Russo-Japanese War">Russo-Japanese War</a> of 1904–1905 limited its threat to the British.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hodge47_131-0"><a href="#cite_note-hodge47-131">[131]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cape_to_Cairo">Cape to Cairo</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_South_Africa_(1815%E2%80%931910)" title="History of South Africa (1815–1910)">History of South Africa (1815–1910)</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_Egypt_under_the_British" title="History of Egypt under the British">History of Egypt under the British</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Scramble_for_Africa" title="Scramble for Africa">Scramble for Africa</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Punch_Rhodes_Colossus.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2681" data-file-width="2069" decoding="async" height="285" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Punch_Rhodes_Colossus.png/220px-Punch_Rhodes_Colossus.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Punch_Rhodes_Colossus.png/330px-Punch_Rhodes_Colossus.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Punch_Rhodes_Colossus.png/440px-Punch_Rhodes_Colossus.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Punch_Rhodes_Colossus.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i><a href="/wiki/The_Rhodes_Colossus" title="The Rhodes Colossus">The Rhodes Colossus</a></i>—<a href="/wiki/Cecil_Rhodes" title="Cecil Rhodes">Cecil Rhodes</a> spanning "Cape to Cairo"</div></div></div>
<p>The Dutch East India Company had founded the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Cape_Colony" title="Dutch Cape Colony">Dutch Cape Colony</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Cape_of_Good_Hope" title="Cape of Good Hope">southern tip of Africa</a> in 1652 as a way station for its ships travelling to and from its colonies in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indies" title="Indies">East Indies</a>. Britain formally acquired the colony, and its large <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Afrikaner" title="Afrikaner">Afrikaner</a> (or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Boer" title="Boer">Boer</a>) population in 1806, having occupied it in 1795 to prevent its falling into French hands during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Flanders_Campaign" title="Flanders Campaign">Flanders Campaign</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> British immigration to the <a href="/wiki/Cape_Colony" title="Cape Colony">Cape Colony</a> began to rise after 1820, and pushed thousands of <a href="/wiki/Boers" title="Boers">Boers</a>, resentful of British rule, northwards to found their own—mostly short-lived—<a href="/wiki/Boer_republics" title="Boer republics">independent republics</a>, during the <a href="/wiki/Great_Trek" title="Great Trek">Great Trek</a> of the late 1830s and early 1840s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> In the process the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voortrekkers" title="Voortrekkers">Voortrekkers</a> clashed repeatedly with the British, who had their own agenda with regard to colonial expansion in South Africa and to the various native African polities, including those of the <a href="/wiki/Sotho_people" title="Sotho people">Sotho people</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Zulu_Kingdom" title="Zulu Kingdom">Zulu Kingdom</a>. Eventually, the Boers established two republics that had a longer lifespan: the <a href="/wiki/South_African_Republic" title="South African Republic">South African Republic</a> or Transvaal Republic (1852–1877; 1881–1902) and the <a href="/wiki/Orange_Free_State" title="Orange Free State">Orange Free State</a> (1854–1902).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup> In 1902 Britain occupied both republics, concluding a treaty with the two <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Boer_Republics" title="Boer Republics">Boer Republics</a> following the <a href="/wiki/Second_Boer_War" title="Second Boer War">Second Boer War</a> (1899–1902).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1869 the <a href="/wiki/Suez_Canal" title="Suez Canal">Suez Canal</a> opened under <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Napoleon_III_of_France" title="Napoleon III of France">Napoleon III</a>, linking the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">Mediterranean Sea</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Ocean" title="Indian Ocean">Indian Ocean</a>. Initially the Canal was opposed by the British;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> but once opened, its strategic value was quickly recognised and became the "jugular vein of the Empire".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup> In 1875, the <a href="/wiki/Conservative_Party_(UK)" title="Conservative Party (UK)">Conservative</a> government of <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Disraeli" title="Benjamin Disraeli">Benjamin Disraeli</a> bought the indebted Egyptian ruler <a href="/wiki/Isma%27il_Pasha" title="Isma'il Pasha">Isma'il Pasha</a>'s 44 per cent shareholding in the Suez Canal for £4 million (equivalent to £400 million in 2021). Although this did not grant outright control of the strategic waterway, it did give Britain leverage. Joint Anglo-French financial control over Egypt ended in outright British occupation in 1882.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2004b230–33_138-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2004b230–33-138">[138]</a></sup>  Although Britain controlled the <a href="/wiki/Khedivate_of_Egypt" title="Khedivate of Egypt">Khedivate of Egypt</a> into the 20th century, it was officially a <a href="/wiki/Vassal_and_tributary_states_of_the_Ottoman_Empire" title="Vassal and tributary states of the Ottoman Empire">vassal state of the Ottoman Empire</a> and not part of the British Empire.  The French were still majority shareholders and attempted to weaken the British position,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> but a compromise was reached with the 1888 <a href="/wiki/Convention_of_Constantinople" title="Convention of Constantinople">Convention of Constantinople</a>, which made the Canal officially neutral territory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup>
</p><p>With competitive French, <a href="/wiki/Belgian_colonial_empire" title="Belgian colonial empire">Belgian</a> and Portuguese activity in the lower <a href="/wiki/Congo_River" title="Congo River">Congo River</a> region undermining orderly colonisation of tropical Africa, the <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Conference" title="Berlin Conference">Berlin Conference</a> of 1884–85 was held to regulate the competition between the European powers in what was called the "<a href="/wiki/Scramble_for_Africa" title="Scramble for Africa">Scramble for Africa</a>" by defining "effective occupation" as the criterion for international recognition of territorial claims.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup> The scramble continued into the 1890s, and caused Britain to reconsider its decision in 1885 to withdraw from <a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">Sudan</a>. A joint force of British and Egyptian troops defeated the <a href="/wiki/Mahdist_War" title="Mahdist War">Mahdist Army</a> in 1896 and rebuffed an attempted French invasion <a href="/wiki/Fashoda_Incident" title="Fashoda Incident">at Fashoda</a> in 1898. Sudan was nominally made an <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Egyptian_Sudan" title="Anglo-Egyptian Sudan">Anglo-Egyptian condominium</a>, but a British colony in reality.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup>
</p><p>British gains in Southern and East Africa prompted <a href="/wiki/Cecil_Rhodes" title="Cecil Rhodes">Cecil Rhodes</a>, pioneer of British expansion in <a href="/wiki/Southern_Africa" title="Southern Africa">Southern Africa</a>, to urge a "<a href="/wiki/Cape_to_Cairo_Railway" title="Cape to Cairo Railway">Cape to Cairo</a>" railway linking the strategically important Suez Canal to the mineral-rich south of the continent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup> During the 1880s and 1890s, Rhodes, with his privately owned <a href="/wiki/British_South_Africa_Company" title="British South Africa Company">British South Africa Company</a>, <a href="/wiki/Company_rule_in_Rhodesia" title="Company rule in Rhodesia">occupied and annexed</a> territories named after him, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rhodesia_(name)" title="Rhodesia (name)">Rhodesia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Changing_status_of_the_white_colonies">Changing status of the white colonies</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dominions" title="Dominions">Dominions</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Confederation" title="Canadian Confederation">Canadian Confederation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Federation_of_Australia" title="Federation of Australia">Federation of Australia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Irish_Home_Rule_movement" title="Irish Home Rule movement">Irish Home Rule movement</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Independence_of_New_Zealand" title="Independence of New Zealand">Independence of New Zealand</a></div>
<p>The path to independence for the white colonies of the British Empire began with the 1839 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Report_on_the_Affairs_of_British_North_America" title="Report on the Affairs of British North America">Durham Report</a>, which proposed unification and self-government for Upper and Lower Canada, as a solution to political unrest which had erupted in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rebellions_of_1837" title="Rebellions of 1837">armed rebellions</a> in 1837.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup> This began with the passing of the <a href="/wiki/Act_of_Union_1840" title="Act of Union 1840">Act of Union</a> in 1840, which created the <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Canada" title="Province of Canada">Province of Canada</a>. <a href="/wiki/Responsible_government" title="Responsible government">Responsible government</a> was first granted to Nova Scotia in 1848, and was soon extended to the other British North American colonies. With the passage of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_North_America_Act,_1867" title="British North America Act, 1867">British North America Act, 1867</a> by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_Parliament" title="British Parliament">British Parliament</a>, the Province of Canada, New Brunswick and Nova Scotia were formed into Canada, a confederation enjoying full self-government with the exception of <a href="/wiki/International_relations" title="International relations">international relations</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup> Australia and New Zealand achieved similar levels of self-government after 1900, with the Australian colonies <a href="/wiki/Federation_of_Australia" title="Federation of Australia">federating in 1901</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup> The term "dominion status" was officially introduced at the <a href="/wiki/1907_Imperial_Conference" title="1907 Imperial Conference">1907 Imperial Conference</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rhodes5_148-0"><a href="#cite_note-rhodes5-148">[148]</a></sup>
</p><p>The last decades of the 19th century saw concerted <a href="/wiki/Political_campaign" title="Political campaign">political campaigns</a> for Irish <a href="/wiki/Home_rule" title="Home rule">home rule</a>. Ireland had been united with Britain into the United Kingdom of Great Britain and Ireland with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Act_of_Union_1800" title="Act of Union 1800">Act of Union 1800</a> after the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Rebellion_of_1798" title="Irish Rebellion of 1798">Irish Rebellion of 1798</a>, and had suffered a severe <a href="/wiki/Great_Famine_(Ireland)" title="Great Famine (Ireland)">famine</a> between 1845 and 1852. Home rule was supported by the British <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Prime Minister of the United Kingdom">Prime minister</a>, <a href="/wiki/William_Ewart_Gladstone" title="William Ewart Gladstone">William Gladstone</a>, who hoped that Ireland might follow in Canada's footsteps as a Dominion within the empire, but his 1886 <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Ireland_Bill_1886" title="Government of Ireland Bill 1886">Home Rule bill</a> was defeated in Parliament. Although the bill, if passed, would have granted Ireland less autonomy within the UK than the Canadian provinces had within their own federation,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup> many MPs feared that a partially independent Ireland might pose a security threat to Great Britain or mark the beginning of the break-up of the empire.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-James,_p._315_150-0"><a href="#cite_note-James,_p._315-150">[150]</a></sup> A <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Irish_Government_Bill_1893" title="Irish Government Bill 1893">second Home Rule bill</a> was defeated for similar reasons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-James,_p._315_150-1"><a href="#cite_note-James,_p._315-150">[150]</a></sup> A <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Home_Rule_Act_1914" title="Home Rule Act 1914">third bill</a> was passed by Parliament in 1914, but not implemented because of the outbreak of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/First_World_War" title="First World War">First World War</a> leading to the 1916 <a href="/wiki/Easter_Rising" title="Easter Rising">Easter Rising</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span id="World_wars_.281914.E2.80.931945.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="World_wars_(1914–1945)">World wars (1914–1945)</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Empire_Needs_Men_WWI.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="407" decoding="async" height="251" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/The_Empire_Needs_Men_WWI.jpg/170px-The_Empire_Needs_Men_WWI.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/The_Empire_Needs_Men_WWI.jpg/255px-The_Empire_Needs_Men_WWI.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/The_Empire_Needs_Men_WWI.jpg/340px-The_Empire_Needs_Men_WWI.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Empire_Needs_Men_WWI.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A poster urging men from countries of the British Empire to enlist</div></div></div>
<p>By the turn of the 20th century, fears had begun to grow in Britain that it would no longer be able to defend the <a href="/wiki/Metropole" title="Metropole">metropole</a> and the entirety of the empire while at the same time maintaining the policy of "splendid isolation".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">Germany</a> was rapidly rising as a military and industrial power and was now seen as the most likely opponent in any future war. Recognising that it was overstretched in the Pacific<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup> and threatened at home by the <a href="/wiki/Imperial_German_Navy" title="Imperial German Navy">Imperial German Navy</a>, Britain <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Japanese_Alliance" title="Anglo-Japanese Alliance">formed an alliance with Japan</a> in 1902 and with its old enemies <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Entente_cordiale" title="Entente cordiale">France</a> and Russia in 1904 and 1907, respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="First_World_War">First World War</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_United_Kingdom_during_the_First_World_War" title="History of the United Kingdom during the First World War">History of the United Kingdom during the First World War</a></div>
<p>Britain's fears of war with Germany were realised in 1914 with the outbreak of the First World War. Britain quickly invaded and occupied most of Germany's overseas colonies in Africa. In the Pacific, Australia and New Zealand occupied <a href="/wiki/German_New_Guinea" title="German New Guinea">German New Guinea</a> and <a href="/wiki/German_Samoa" title="German Samoa">German Samoa</a> respectively. Plans for a post-war division of the Ottoman Empire, which had joined the war on Germany's side, were secretly drawn up by Britain and France under the 1916 <a href="/wiki/Sykes%E2%80%93Picot_Agreement" title="Sykes–Picot Agreement">Sykes–Picot Agreement</a>. This agreement was not divulged to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hussein_bin_Ali,_Sharif_of_Mecca" title="Hussein bin Ali, Sharif of Mecca">Sharif of Mecca</a>, who the British had been encouraging to launch an Arab revolt against their Ottoman rulers, giving the impression that Britain was supporting the creation of an independent Arab state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brown494-495_155-0"><a href="#cite_note-Brown494-495-155">[155]</a></sup>
</p><p>The British declaration of war on Germany and its allies committed the colonies and Dominions, which provided invaluable military, financial and material support. Over 2.5 million men served in the armies of the <a href="/wiki/Dominion" title="Dominion">Dominions</a>, as well as many thousands of volunteers from the Crown colonies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup> The contributions of Australian and New Zealand troops during the 1915 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gallipoli_Campaign" title="Gallipoli Campaign">Gallipoli Campaign</a> against the Ottoman Empire had a great impact on the national consciousness at home and marked a watershed in the transition of Australia and New Zealand from colonies to nations in their own right. The countries continue to commemorate this occasion on <a href="/wiki/Anzac_Day" title="Anzac Day">Anzac Day</a>. Canadians viewed the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Vimy_Ridge" title="Battle of Vimy Ridge">Battle of Vimy Ridge</a> in a similar light.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup> The important contribution of the Dominions to the <a href="/wiki/War_effort" title="War effort">war effort</a> was recognised in 1917 by the British Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/David_Lloyd_George" title="David Lloyd George">David Lloyd George</a> when he invited each of the Dominion Prime Ministers to join an <a href="/wiki/Imperial_War_Cabinet" title="Imperial War Cabinet">Imperial War Cabinet</a> to co-ordinate imperial policy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup>
</p><p>Under the terms of the concluding <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Versailles" title="Treaty of Versailles">Treaty of Versailles</a> signed in 1919, the empire reached its greatest extent with the addition of 1.8 million sq mi (4.7 million km<sup>2</sup>) and 13 million new subjects.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2004b315_159-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2004b315-159">[159]</a></sup> The colonies of Germany and the Ottoman Empire were distributed to the Allied powers as <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations_mandate" title="League of Nations mandate">League of Nations mandates</a>. Britain gained control of <a href="/wiki/Mandatory_Palestine" title="Mandatory Palestine">Palestine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Emirate_of_Transjordan" title="Emirate of Transjordan">Transjordan</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Iraq_(Mandate_administration)" title="Kingdom of Iraq (Mandate administration)">Iraq</a>, parts of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_Cameroons" title="British Cameroons">Cameroon</a> and <a href="/wiki/British_Togoland" title="British Togoland">Togoland</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tanganyika_(territory)" title="Tanganyika (territory)">Tanganyika</a>. The Dominions themselves acquired mandates of their own: the <a href="/wiki/Union_of_South_Africa" title="Union of South Africa">Union of South Africa</a> gained South West Africa (modern-day <a href="/wiki/Namibia" title="Namibia">Namibia</a>), Australia gained <a href="/wiki/Territory_of_New_Guinea" title="Territory of New Guinea">New Guinea</a>, and New Zealand <a href="/wiki/Western_Samoa_Trust_Territory" title="Western Samoa Trust Territory">Western Samoa</a>. <a href="/wiki/History_of_Nauru#World_War_I_to_World_War_II" title="History of Nauru">Nauru</a> was made a combined mandate of Britain and the two Pacific Dominions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Inter-war_period">Inter-war period</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Interwar_Britain" title="Interwar Britain">Interwar Britain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Irish_revolutionary_period" title="Irish revolutionary period">Irish revolutionary period</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indian_independence_movement" title="Indian independence movement">Indian independence movement</a>, <a href="/wiki/Partition_of_the_Ottoman_Empire" title="Partition of the Ottoman Empire">Partition of the Ottoman Empire</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:British_Empire_1921.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="625" data-file-width="1425" decoding="async" height="175" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/British_Empire_1921.png/400px-British_Empire_1921.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/British_Empire_1921.png/600px-British_Empire_1921.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/British_Empire_1921.png/800px-British_Empire_1921.png 2x" width="400"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:British_Empire_1921.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The British Empire at its territorial peak in 1921</div></div></div>
<p>The changing world order that the war had brought about, in particular the growth of the United States and Japan as naval powers, and the rise of independence movements in India and Ireland, caused a major reassessment of British imperial policy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup> Forced to choose between alignment with the United States or Japan, Britain opted not to renew its <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Japanese_Alliance" title="Anglo-Japanese Alliance">Anglo-Japanese Alliance</a> and instead signed the 1922 <a href="/wiki/Washington_Naval_Treaty" title="Washington Naval Treaty">Washington Naval Treaty</a>, where Britain accepted naval parity with the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reflouis302_162-0"><a href="#cite_note-reflouis302-162">[162]</a></sup> This decision was the source of much debate in Britain during the 1930s<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup> as militaristic governments took hold in Germany and Japan helped in part by the <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a>, for it was feared that the empire could not survive a simultaneous attack by both nations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup> The issue of the empire's security was a serious concern in Britain, as it was vital to the <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Economy of the United Kingdom">British economy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1919, the frustrations caused by delays to <a href="/wiki/Irish_Home_Rule_movement" title="Irish Home Rule movement">Irish home rule</a> led the MPs of <a href="/wiki/Sinn_F%C3%A9in" title="Sinn Féin">Sinn Féin</a>, a pro-independence party that had won a majority of the Irish seats in the <a href="/wiki/1918_Irish_general_election" title="1918 Irish general election">1918 British general election</a>, to establish an <a href="/wiki/D%C3%A1il_%C3%89ireann_(Irish_Republic)" title="Dáil Éireann (Irish Republic)">independent parliament</a> in <a href="/wiki/Dublin" title="Dublin">Dublin</a>, at which <a href="/wiki/Irish_Declaration_of_Independence" title="Irish Declaration of Independence">Irish independence was declared</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Irish_Republican_Army" title="Irish Republican Army">Irish Republican Army</a> simultaneously began a <a href="/wiki/Guerrilla_warfare" title="Guerrilla warfare">guerrilla war</a> against the British administration.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Irish_War_of_Independence" title="Irish War of Independence">Irish War of Independence</a> ended in 1921 with a stalemate and the signing of the <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Irish_Treaty" title="Anglo-Irish Treaty">Anglo-Irish Treaty</a>, creating the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Free_State" title="Irish Free State">Irish Free State</a>, a Dominion within the British Empire, with effective internal independence but still constitutionally linked with the British Crown.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a>, consisting of six of the 32 <a href="/wiki/Counties_of_Ireland" title="Counties of Ireland">Irish counties</a> which had been established as a devolved region under the 1920 <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Ireland_Act_1920" title="Government of Ireland Act 1920">Government of Ireland Act</a>, immediately exercised its option under the treaty to retain its existing status within the United Kingdom.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ImperialConference.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="506" data-file-width="635" decoding="async" height="175" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/ImperialConference.jpg/220px-ImperialConference.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/ImperialConference.jpg/330px-ImperialConference.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/ImperialConference.jpg/440px-ImperialConference.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ImperialConference.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/George_V" title="George V">George V</a> with British and Dominion prime ministers at the <a href="/wiki/1926_Imperial_Conference" title="1926 Imperial Conference">1926 Imperial Conference</a></div></div></div>
<p>A similar struggle began in India when the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_India_Act_1919" title="Government of India Act 1919">Government of India Act 1919</a> failed to satisfy the demand for independence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2004b330_169-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2004b330-169">[169]</a></sup> Concerns over communist and foreign plots following the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ghadar_conspiracy" title="Ghadar conspiracy">Ghadar conspiracy</a> ensured that war-time strictures were renewed by the <a href="/wiki/Rowlatt_Act" title="Rowlatt Act">Rowlatt Acts</a>. This led to tension,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-refjames416_170-0"><a href="#cite_note-refjames416-170">[170]</a></sup> particularly in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Punjab_region" title="Punjab region">Punjab region</a>, where repressive measures culminated in the <a href="/wiki/Jallianwala_Bagh_massacre" title="Jallianwala Bagh massacre">Amritsar Massacre</a>. In Britain, public opinion was divided over the morality of the massacre, between those who saw it as having saved India from anarchy, and those who viewed it with revulsion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-refjames416_170-1"><a href="#cite_note-refjames416-170">[170]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Non-cooperation_movement" title="Non-cooperation movement">non-cooperation movement</a> was called off in March 1922 following the <a href="/wiki/Chauri_Chaura_incident" title="Chauri Chaura incident">Chauri Chaura incident</a>, and discontent continued to simmer for the next 25 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1922, Egypt, which had been declared a British <a href="/wiki/Protectorate" title="Protectorate">protectorate</a> at the outbreak of the First World War, was <a href="/wiki/Unilateral_Declaration_of_Egyptian_Independence" title="Unilateral Declaration of Egyptian Independence">granted formal independence</a>, though it continued to be a British client state until 1954. <a href="/wiki/British_Army" title="British Army">British troops</a> remained stationed in Egypt until the signing of the <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Egyptian_treaty_of_1936" title="Anglo-Egyptian treaty of 1936">Anglo-Egyptian Treaty</a> in 1936,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup> under which it was agreed that the troops would withdraw but continue to occupy and defend the Suez Canal zone. In return, Egypt was assisted in joining the <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">League of Nations</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup> Iraq, a British mandate since 1920, gained membership of the League in its own right after achieving independence from Britain in 1932.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup> In Palestine, Britain was presented with the problem of mediating between the Arabs and increasing numbers of Jews. The <a href="/wiki/Balfour_Declaration" title="Balfour Declaration">Balfour Declaration</a>, which had been incorporated into the terms of the mandate, stated that a national home for the Jewish people would be established in Palestine, and Jewish immigration allowed up to a limit that would be determined by the mandatory power.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup> This led to increasing conflict with the Arab population, who openly <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1936%E2%80%9339_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine" title="1936–39 Arab revolt in Palestine">revolted in 1936</a>. As the threat of war with Germany increased during the 1930s, Britain judged the support of Arabs as more important than the establishment of a Jewish homeland, and shifted to a pro-Arab stance, limiting Jewish immigration and in turn triggering a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jewish_insurgency_in_Palestine" title="Jewish insurgency in Palestine">Jewish insurgency</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brown494-495_155-1"><a href="#cite_note-Brown494-495-155">[155]</a></sup>
</p><p>The right of the Dominions to set their own foreign policy, independent of Britain, was recognised at the <a href="/wiki/1923_Imperial_Conference" title="1923 Imperial Conference">1923 Imperial Conference</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup> Britain's request for military assistance from the Dominions at the outbreak of the <a href="/wiki/Chanak_Crisis" title="Chanak Crisis">Chanak Crisis</a> the previous year had been turned down by Canada and South Africa, and Canada had refused to be bound by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Lausanne_(1923)" title="Treaty of Lausanne (1923)">1923 Treaty of Lausanne</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup> After pressure from the Irish Free State and South Africa, the <a href="/wiki/1926_Imperial_Conference" title="1926 Imperial Conference">1926 Imperial Conference</a> issued the <a href="/wiki/Balfour_Declaration_of_1926" title="Balfour Declaration of 1926">Balfour Declaration of 1926</a>, declaring the Dominions to be "autonomous Communities within the British Empire, equal in status, in no way subordinate one to another" within a "British Commonwealth of Nations".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179"><a href="#cite_note-179">[179]</a></sup> This declaration was given legal substance under the 1931 <a href="/wiki/Statute_of_Westminster_1931" title="Statute of Westminster 1931">Statute of Westminster</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rhodes5_148-1"><a href="#cite_note-rhodes5-148">[148]</a></sup> The parliaments of Canada, Australia, New Zealand, the Union of South Africa, the Irish Free State and <a href="/wiki/Dominion_of_Newfoundland" title="Dominion of Newfoundland">Newfoundland</a> were now independent of British legislative control, they could nullify <a href="/wiki/Law_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Law of the United Kingdom">British laws</a> and Britain could no longer pass laws for them without their consent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup> Newfoundland reverted to colonial status in 1933, suffering from financial difficulties during the Great Depression.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup> In 1937 the Irish Free State introduced a <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Ireland" title="Constitution of Ireland">republican constitution</a> renaming itself <i>Ireland</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Second_World_War">Second World War</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/British_Empire_in_World_War_II" title="British Empire in World War II">British Empire in World War II</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:El_Alamein_1942_-_British_infantry.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1772" data-file-width="1784" decoding="async" height="219" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/El_Alamein_1942_-_British_infantry.jpg/220px-El_Alamein_1942_-_British_infantry.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/El_Alamein_1942_-_British_infantry.jpg/330px-El_Alamein_1942_-_British_infantry.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/El_Alamein_1942_-_British_infantry.jpg/440px-El_Alamein_1942_-_British_infantry.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:El_Alamein_1942_-_British_infantry.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>During the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Second_World_War" title="Second World War">Second World War</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Eighth_Army_(United_Kingdom)" title="Eighth Army (United Kingdom)">Eighth Army</a> was made up of units from many different countries in the British Empire and Commonwealth; it fought in the <a href="/wiki/North_African_campaign" title="North African campaign">North African</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_Campaign_(World_War_II)" title="Italian Campaign (World War II)">Italian</a> campaigns.</div></div></div>
<p>Britain's declaration of war against <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi Germany</a> in September 1939 included the Crown colonies and India but did not automatically commit the Dominions of Australia, Canada, New Zealand, Newfoundland and South Africa. All soon declared war on Germany. While Britain continued to regard Ireland as still within the British Commonwealth, Ireland chose to remain <a href="/wiki/Irish_neutrality_during_World_War_II" title="Irish neutrality during World War II">legally neutral</a> throughout <a href="/wiki/The_Emergency_(Ireland)" title="The Emergency (Ireland)">the war</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup>
</p><p>After the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fall_of_France" title="Fall of France">Fall of France</a> in June 1940, Britain and the empire stood alone against Germany, until the <a href="/wiki/German_invasion_of_Greece" title="German invasion of Greece">German invasion of Greece</a> on 7 April 1941. British Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Winston_Churchill" title="Winston Churchill">Winston Churchill</a> successfully lobbied President <a href="/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt" title="Franklin D. Roosevelt">Franklin D. Roosevelt</a> for <a href="/wiki/Military_aid" title="Military aid">military aid</a> from the United States, but Roosevelt was not yet ready to ask <a href="/wiki/United_States_Congress" title="United States Congress">Congress</a> to commit the country to war.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup> In August 1941, Churchill and Roosevelt met and signed the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Charter" title="Atlantic Charter">Atlantic Charter</a>, which included the statement that "the rights of all peoples to choose the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Form_of_government" title="Form of government">form of government</a> under which they live" should be respected. This wording was ambiguous as to whether it referred to European countries invaded by Germany and Italy, or the peoples colonised by European nations, and would later be interpreted differently by the British, Americans, and nationalist movements.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reflloyd316_185-0"><a href="#cite_note-reflloyd316-185">[185]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186"><a href="#cite_note-186">[186]</a></sup>
</p><p>For Churchill, the entry of the United States into the war was the "greatest joy".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187"><a href="#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup> He felt that Britain was now assured of victory,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup> but failed to recognise that the "many disasters, immeasurable costs and tribulations [which he knew] lay ahead"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189"><a href="#cite_note-189">[189]</a></sup> in December 1941 would have permanent consequences for the future of the empire. The manner in which British forces were rapidly defeated in the Far East irreversibly harmed Britain's standing and prestige as an imperial power,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190"><a href="#cite_note-190">[190]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191"><a href="#cite_note-191">[191]</a></sup> including, particularly, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Battle_of_Singapore" title="Battle of Singapore">Fall of Singapore</a>, which had previously been hailed as an impregnable fortress and the eastern equivalent of Gibraltar.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192"><a href="#cite_note-192">[192]</a></sup> The realisation that Britain could not defend its entire empire pushed Australia and New Zealand, which now appeared threatened by Japanese forces, into closer ties with the United States and, ultimately, the 1951 <a href="/wiki/ANZUS" title="ANZUS">ANZUS Pact</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reflloyd316_185-1"><a href="#cite_note-reflloyd316-185">[185]</a></sup> The war weakened the empire in other ways: undermining Britain's control of politics in India, inflicting long-term economic damage, and irrevocably changing geopolitics by pushing the Soviet Union and the United States to the centre of the global stage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193"><a href="#cite_note-193">[193]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span id="Decolonisation_and_decline_.281945.E2.80.931997.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Decolonisation_and_decline_(1945–1997)">Decolonisation and decline (1945–1997)</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Decolonization" title="Decolonization">Decolonization</a></div>
<p><span class="anchor" id="Decolonisation"></span><span class="anchor" id="Decolonization"></span><span class="anchor" id="Decline"></span>
Though Britain and the empire emerged victorious from the Second World War, the effects of the conflict were profound, both at home and abroad. Much of Europe, a continent that had dominated the world for several centuries, was in ruins, and host to the armies of the United States and the Soviet Union, who now held the balance of global power.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194"><a href="#cite_note-194">[194]</a></sup> Britain was left essentially bankrupt, with insolvency only averted in 1946 after the negotiation of <a href="/wiki/Anglo-American_loan" title="Anglo-American loan">a US$4.33 billion loan</a> from the United States,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-195"><a href="#cite_note-195">[195]</a></sup> the last installment of which was repaid in 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GT-DEX-2006-33_196-0"><a href="#cite_note-GT-DEX-2006-33-196">[196]</a></sup> At the same time, anti-colonial movements were on the rise in the colonies of European nations. The situation was complicated further by the increasing <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a> rivalry of the United States and the Soviet Union. In principle, both nations were opposed to European colonialism. In practice, American <a href="/wiki/Anti-communism" title="Anti-communism">anti-communism</a> prevailed over <a href="/wiki/Anti-imperialism" title="Anti-imperialism">anti-imperialism</a>, and therefore the United States supported the continued existence of the British Empire to keep Communist expansion in check.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-197"><a href="#cite_note-197">[197]</a></sup> At first British politicians believed it would be possible to maintain Britain's role as a world power at the head of a re-imagined Commonwealth,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-198"><a href="#cite_note-198">[198]</a></sup> but by 1960 they were forced to recognise that there was an irresistible "<a href="/wiki/Wind_of_Change_(speech)" title="Wind of Change (speech)">wind of change</a>" blowing. Their priorities changed to maintaining an extensive zone of British influence<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-199"><a href="#cite_note-199">[199]</a></sup> and ensuring that stable, non-Communist governments were established in former colonies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Heinlein2002_200-0"><a href="#cite_note-Heinlein2002-200">[200]</a></sup> In this context, while other European powers such as France and Portugal waged costly and unsuccessful wars to keep their empires intact, Britain generally adopted a policy of peaceful disengagement from its colonies, although violence occurred in Malaya, Kenya and Palestine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-201"><a href="#cite_note-201">[201]</a></sup> Between 1945 and 1965, the number of people under British rule outside the UK itself fell from 700 million to 5 million, 3 million of whom were in Hong Kong.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-202"><a href="#cite_note-202">[202]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Initial_disengagement">Initial disengagement</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Partition_of_India" title="Partition of India">Partition of India</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1947%E2%80%931949_Palestine_war" title="1947–1949 Palestine war">1947–1949 Palestine war</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Malayan_Emergency" title="Malayan Emergency">Malayan Emergency</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Emergency_trains_crowded_with_desperate_refugees.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="424" data-file-width="600" decoding="async" height="155" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Emergency_trains_crowded_with_desperate_refugees.jpg/220px-Emergency_trains_crowded_with_desperate_refugees.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Emergency_trains_crowded_with_desperate_refugees.jpg/330px-Emergency_trains_crowded_with_desperate_refugees.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Emergency_trains_crowded_with_desperate_refugees.jpg/440px-Emergency_trains_crowded_with_desperate_refugees.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Emergency_trains_crowded_with_desperate_refugees.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>About 14.5 million people lost their homes as a result of the <a href="/wiki/Partition_of_India" title="Partition of India">partition of India</a> in 1947.</div></div></div>
<p>The pro-decolonisation <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">Labour</a> government, elected at the <a href="/wiki/1945_United_Kingdom_general_election" title="1945 United Kingdom general election">1945 general election</a> and led by <a href="/wiki/Clement_Attlee" title="Clement Attlee">Clement Attlee</a>, moved quickly to tackle the most pressing issue facing the empire: <a href="/wiki/Indian_independence_movement" title="Indian independence movement">Indian independence</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-203"><a href="#cite_note-203">[203]</a></sup> India's two major political parties—the <a href="/wiki/Indian_National_Congress" title="Indian National Congress">Indian National Congress</a> (led by <a href="/wiki/Mahatma_Gandhi" title="Mahatma Gandhi">Mahatma Gandhi</a>) and the <a href="/wiki/All-India_Muslim_League" title="All-India Muslim League">Muslim League</a> (led by <a href="/wiki/Muhammad_Ali_Jinnah" title="Muhammad Ali Jinnah">Muhammad Ali Jinnah</a>)—had been campaigning for independence for decades, but disagreed as to how it should be implemented. Congress favoured a unified secular Indian state, whereas the League, fearing domination by the Hindu majority, desired a separate <a href="/wiki/Islamic_state" title="Islamic state">Islamic state</a> for Muslim-majority regions. Increasing <a href="/wiki/Civil_disorder" title="Civil disorder">civil unrest</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Indian_Navy_mutiny" title="Royal Indian Navy mutiny">mutiny</a> of the <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Indian_Navy" title="History of the Indian Navy">Royal Indian Navy</a> during 1946 led Attlee to promise independence no later than 30 June 1948. When the urgency of the situation and risk of civil war became apparent, the newly appointed (and last) Viceroy, <a href="/wiki/Louis_Mountbatten,_1st_Earl_Mountbatten_of_Burma" title="Louis Mountbatten, 1st Earl Mountbatten of Burma">Lord Mountbatten</a>, hastily brought forward the date to 15 August 1947.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-204"><a href="#cite_note-204">[204]</a></sup> The borders drawn by the British to broadly <a href="/wiki/Partition_of_India" title="Partition of India">partition India</a> into Hindu and Muslim areas left tens of millions as minorities in the newly independent states of India and <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-205"><a href="#cite_note-205">[205]</a></sup> Millions of Muslims crossed from India to Pakistan and Hindus vice versa, and violence between the two communities cost hundreds of thousands of lives. Burma, which had been administered as part of the British Raj, and Sri Lanka gained their independence the following year in 1948. India, Pakistan and Sri Lanka became members of the Commonwealth, while Burma chose not to join.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-206"><a href="#cite_note-206">[206]</a></sup>
</p><p>The British Mandate in Palestine, where an Arab majority lived alongside a Jewish minority, presented the British with a similar problem to that of India.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-207"><a href="#cite_note-207">[207]</a></sup> The matter was complicated by large numbers of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jewish_refugees" title="Jewish refugees">Jewish refugees</a> seeking to be admitted to Palestine following the <a href="/wiki/The_Holocaust" title="The Holocaust">Holocaust</a>, while Arabs were opposed to the creation of a Jewish state. Frustrated by the intractability of the problem, attacks by Jewish paramilitary organisations and the increasing cost of maintaining its military presence, Britain announced in 1947 that it would withdraw in 1948 and leave the matter to the United Nations to solve.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-208"><a href="#cite_note-208">[208]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly" title="United Nations General Assembly">UN General Assembly</a> subsequently voted for a <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Partition_Plan_for_Palestine" title="United Nations Partition Plan for Palestine">plan to partition Palestine</a> into a Jewish and an Arab state. It was immediately followed by the outbreak of a <a href="/wiki/1947%E2%80%931948_civil_war_in_Mandatory_Palestine" title="1947–1948 civil war in Mandatory Palestine">civil war</a> between the Arabs and Jews of Palestine, and British forces withdrew amid the fighting. The British Mandate for Palestine officially terminated at midnight on 15 May 1948 as the State of <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a> declared independence and the <a href="/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War" title="1948 Arab–Israeli War">1948 Arab-Israeli War</a> broke out, during which the territory of the former Mandate was partitioned between Israel and the surrounding Arab states. Amid the fighting, British forces continued to withdraw from Israel, with the last British troops departing from <a href="/wiki/Haifa" title="Haifa">Haifa</a> on 30 June 1948.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-209"><a href="#cite_note-209">[209]</a></sup>
</p><p>Following the <a href="/wiki/Surrender_of_Japan" title="Surrender of Japan">surrender of Japan</a> in the Second World War, anti-Japanese <a href="/wiki/Resistance_movement" title="Resistance movement">resistance movements</a> in Malaya turned their attention towards the British, who had moved to quickly retake control of the colony, valuing it as a source of rubber and tin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_210-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-210">[210]</a></sup> The fact that the guerrillas were primarily <a href="/wiki/Malaysian_Chinese" title="Malaysian Chinese">Malaysian Chinese</a> Communists meant that the British attempt to quell the uprising was supported by the <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Malaysia" title="Islam in Malaysia">Muslim Malay</a> majority, on the understanding that once the insurgency had been quelled, independence would be granted.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_210-1"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-210">[210]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Malayan_Emergency" title="Malayan Emergency">Malayan Emergency</a>, as it was called, began in 1948 and lasted until 1960, but by 1957, Britain felt confident enough to grant independence to the <a href="/wiki/Federation_of_Malaya" title="Federation of Malaya">Federation of Malaya</a> within the Commonwealth. In 1963, the 11 states of the federation together with Singapore, Sarawak and <a href="/wiki/Crown_Colony_of_North_Borneo" title="Crown Colony of North Borneo">North Borneo</a> joined to form <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a>, but in 1965 Chinese-majority <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a> was expelled from the union following tensions between the Malay and Chinese populations and became an independent city-state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-211"><a href="#cite_note-211">[211]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Brunei" title="Brunei">Brunei</a>, which had been a British protectorate since 1888, declined to join the union.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-212"><a href="#cite_note-212">[212]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Suez_and_its_aftermath">Suez and its aftermath</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Suez_Crisis" title="Suez Crisis">Suez Crisis</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Anthony_Eden_(retouched).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1300" data-file-width="968" decoding="async" height="228" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Anthony_Eden_%28retouched%29.jpg/170px-Anthony_Eden_%28retouched%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Anthony_Eden_%28retouched%29.jpg/255px-Anthony_Eden_%28retouched%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Anthony_Eden_%28retouched%29.jpg/340px-Anthony_Eden_%28retouched%29.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Anthony_Eden_(retouched).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Anthony_Eden" title="Anthony Eden">Eden</a>'s decision to invade <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a> in 1956 revealed Britain's post-war weaknesses.</div></div></div>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/1951_United_Kingdom_general_election" title="1951 United Kingdom general election">1951 general election</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Conservative_Party_(UK)" title="Conservative Party (UK)">Conservative Party</a> returned to power in Britain under the leadership of Winston Churchill. Churchill and the Conservatives believed that Britain's position as a world power relied on the continued existence of the empire, with the base at the Suez Canal allowing Britain to maintain its pre-eminent position in the Middle East in spite of the loss of India. Churchill could not ignore <a href="/wiki/Gamal_Abdel_Nasser" title="Gamal Abdel Nasser">Gamal Abdul Nasser</a>'s new revolutionary <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Egypt" title="Politics of Egypt">government of Egypt</a> that had <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Egyptian_Revolution_of_1952" title="Egyptian Revolution of 1952">taken power in 1952</a>, and the following year it was agreed that British troops would withdraw from the Suez Canal zone and that Sudan would be granted self-determination by 1955, with independence to follow.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-213"><a href="#cite_note-213">[213]</a></sup> Sudan was <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/History_of_Sudan_(1956%E2%80%9369)" title="History of Sudan (1956–69)">granted independence</a> on 1 January 1956.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-214"><a href="#cite_note-214">[214]</a></sup>
</p><p>In July 1956, Nasser unilaterally nationalised the Suez Canal. The response of <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Eden" title="Anthony Eden">Anthony Eden</a>, who had succeeded Churchill as Prime Minister, was to collude with France to engineer an Israeli attack on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Republic_of_Egypt_(1953%E2%80%9358)" title="Republic of Egypt (1953–58)">Egypt</a> that would give Britain and France an excuse to intervene militarily and retake the canal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-215"><a href="#cite_note-215">[215]</a></sup> Eden infuriated US President <a href="/wiki/Dwight_D._Eisenhower" title="Dwight D. Eisenhower">Dwight D. Eisenhower</a> by his lack of consultation, and Eisenhower refused to back the invasion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2004b355_216-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2004b355-216">[216]</a></sup> Another of Eisenhower's concerns was the possibility of a wider war with the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> after it threatened to intervene on the Egyptian side. Eisenhower applied <a href="/wiki/Leverage_(finance)" title="Leverage (finance)">financial leverage</a> by threatening to sell US reserves of the <a href="/wiki/Pound_sterling" title="Pound sterling">British pound</a> and thereby precipitate a collapse of the British currency.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2004b356_217-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2004b356-217">[217]</a></sup> Though the invasion force was militarily successful in its objectives,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-218"><a href="#cite_note-218">[218]</a></sup> UN intervention and US pressure forced Britain into a humiliating withdrawal of its forces, and Eden resigned.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-219"><a href="#cite_note-219">[219]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-220"><a href="#cite_note-220">[220]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Suez_Crisis" title="Suez Crisis">Suez Crisis</a> very publicly exposed Britain's limitations to the world and confirmed Britain's decline on the world stage and its end as a first-rate power,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-221"><a href="#cite_note-221">[221]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-222"><a href="#cite_note-222">[222]</a></sup> demonstrating that henceforth it could no longer act without at least the acquiescence, if not the full support, of the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-223"><a href="#cite_note-223">[223]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-224"><a href="#cite_note-224">[224]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-225"><a href="#cite_note-225">[225]</a></sup> The events at Suez wounded British <a href="/wiki/Patriotism" title="Patriotism">national pride</a>, leading one <a href="/wiki/Member_of_Parliament_(United_Kingdom)" title="Member of Parliament (United Kingdom)">Member of Parliament</a> (MP) to describe it as "Britain's <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Waterloo" title="Battle of Waterloo">Waterloo</a>"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-#refOHBEv4|Brown,_p._343_226-0"><a href="#cite_note-#refOHBEv4|Brown,_p._343-226">[226]</a></sup> and another to suggest that the country had become an "American <a href="/wiki/Satellite_state" title="Satellite state">satellite</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-227"><a href="#cite_note-227">[227]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Margaret_Thatcher" title="Margaret Thatcher">Margaret Thatcher</a> later described the mindset she believed had befallen Britain's political leaders after Suez where they "went from believing that Britain could do anything to an almost neurotic belief that Britain could do nothing", from which Britain did not recover until the successful recapture of the <a href="/wiki/Falkland_Islands" title="Falkland Islands">Falkland Islands</a> from Argentina in 1982.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-228"><a href="#cite_note-228">[228]</a></sup>
</p><p>While the Suez Crisis caused British power in the Middle East to weaken, it did not collapse.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-229"><a href="#cite_note-229">[229]</a></sup> Britain again deployed its armed forces to the region, intervening in <a href="/wiki/Muscat_and_Oman" title="Muscat and Oman">Oman</a> (<a href="/wiki/Jebel_Akhdar_War" title="Jebel Akhdar War">1957</a>), <a href="/wiki/Jordan" title="Jordan">Jordan</a> (<a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_127" title="United Nations Security Council Resolution 127">1958</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Sheikhdom_of_Kuwait" title="Sheikhdom of Kuwait">Kuwait</a> (<a href="/wiki/Operation_Vantage" title="Operation Vantage">1961</a>), though on these occasions with American approval,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-230"><a href="#cite_note-230">[230]</a></sup> as the new Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Harold_Macmillan" title="Harold Macmillan">Harold Macmillan</a>'s foreign policy was to remain firmly aligned with the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-#refOHBEv4|Brown,_p._343_226-1"><a href="#cite_note-#refOHBEv4|Brown,_p._343-226">[226]</a></sup> Although Britain granted Kuwait independence in 1961, it continued to maintain a military presence in the Middle East for another decade. On 16 January 1968, a few weeks after the <a href="/wiki/Pound_sterling#Bretton_Woods" title="Pound sterling">devaluation of the pound</a>, Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Harold_Wilson" title="Harold Wilson">Harold Wilson</a> and his <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State_for_Defence" title="Secretary of State for Defence">Defence Secretary</a> <a href="/wiki/Denis_Healey" title="Denis Healey">Denis Healey</a> announced that <a href="/wiki/British_Armed_Forces" title="British Armed Forces">British Armed Forces</a> troops would be withdrawn from major military bases <a href="/wiki/East_of_Suez" title="East of Suez">East of Suez</a>, which included the ones in the Middle East, and primarily from Malaysia and Singapore by the end of 1971, instead of 1975 as earlier planned.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-231"><a href="#cite_note-231">[231]</a></sup> By that time over 50,000 British military personnel were still stationed in the Far East, including 30,000 in Singapore.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-232"><a href="#cite_note-232">[232]</a></sup> The British granted independence to the <a href="/wiki/Maldives" title="Maldives">Maldives</a> in 1965 but continued to station a garrison there until 1976, withdrew from <a href="/wiki/South_Yemen" title="South Yemen">Aden</a> in 1967, and granted independence to <a href="/wiki/Bahrain" title="Bahrain">Bahrain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Qatar" title="Qatar">Qatar</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates" title="United Arab Emirates">United Arab Emirates</a> in 1971.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-233"><a href="#cite_note-233">[233]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wind_of_change">Wind of change</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Decolonisation_of_Africa" title="Decolonisation of Africa">Decolonisation of Africa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Decolonization_of_Asia" title="Decolonization of Asia">Decolonization of Asia</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Wind_of_Change_(speech)" title="Wind of Change (speech)">Wind of Change (speech)</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:British_Decolonisation_in_Africa.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="2000" decoding="async" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/British_Decolonisation_in_Africa.png/220px-British_Decolonisation_in_Africa.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/British_Decolonisation_in_Africa.png/330px-British_Decolonisation_in_Africa.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/British_Decolonisation_in_Africa.png/440px-British_Decolonisation_in_Africa.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:British_Decolonisation_in_Africa.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>British decolonisation in Africa. By the end of the 1960s, all but <a href="/wiki/Rhodesia" title="Rhodesia">Rhodesia</a> (the future Zimbabwe) and the South African mandate of South West Africa (Namibia) had achieved recognised independence.</div></div></div>
<p>Macmillan gave a speech in <a href="/wiki/Cape_Town" title="Cape Town">Cape Town</a>, South Africa in February 1960 where he spoke of "the wind of change blowing through this continent".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-234"><a href="#cite_note-234">[234]</a></sup> Macmillan wished to avoid the same kind of <a href="/wiki/Algerian_War" title="Algerian War">colonial war</a> that France was fighting in <a href="/wiki/French_Algeria" title="French Algeria">Algeria</a>, and under his premiership decolonisation proceeded rapidly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-235"><a href="#cite_note-235">[235]</a></sup> To the three colonies that had been granted independence in the 1950s—Sudan, the <a href="/wiki/Gold_Coast_(British_colony)" title="Gold Coast (British colony)">Gold Coast</a> and Malaya—were added nearly ten times that number during the 1960s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-236"><a href="#cite_note-236">[236]</a></sup>
</p><p>Britain's remaining colonies in Africa, except for <a href="/wiki/Self-governing_colony" title="Self-governing colony">self-governing</a> <a href="/wiki/Southern_Rhodesia" title="Southern Rhodesia">Southern Rhodesia</a>, were all granted independence by 1968. British withdrawal from the southern and eastern parts of Africa was not a peaceful process. Kenyan independence was preceded by the eight-year <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mau_Mau_uprising" title="Mau Mau uprising">Mau Mau uprising</a>, in which tens of thousands of suspected rebels were interned by the colonial government in detention camps.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-237"><a href="#cite_note-237">[237]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Rhodesia" title="Rhodesia">Rhodesia</a>, the 1965 <a href="/wiki/Rhodesia%27s_Unilateral_Declaration_of_Independence" title="Rhodesia's Unilateral Declaration of Independence">Unilateral Declaration of Independence</a> by the white minority resulted in a <a href="/wiki/Rhodesian_Bush_War" title="Rhodesian Bush War">civil war</a> that lasted until the <a href="/wiki/Lancaster_House_Agreement" title="Lancaster House Agreement">Lancaster House Agreement</a> of 1979, which set the terms for recognised independence in 1980, as the new nation of <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe" title="Zimbabwe">Zimbabwe</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-238"><a href="#cite_note-238">[238]</a></sup>
