</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">Cyprus</a>, a guerrilla war waged by the <a href="/wiki/Greek_Cypriots" title="Greek Cypriots">Greek Cypriot</a> organisation <a href="/wiki/EOKA" title="EOKA">EOKA</a> against British rule, was ended in 1959 by the <a href="/wiki/London_and_Z%C3%BCrich_Agreements" title="London and Zürich Agreements">London and Zürich Agreements</a>, which resulted in Cyprus being granted independence in 1960. The UK retained the military bases of <a href="/wiki/Akrotiri_and_Dhekelia" title="Akrotiri and Dhekelia">Akrotiri and Dhekelia</a> as sovereign base areas. The <a href="/wiki/List_of_islands_in_the_Mediterranean" title="List of islands in the Mediterranean">Mediterranean</a> colony of <a href="/wiki/Malta_(island)" title="Malta (island)">Malta</a> was amicably granted independence from the UK in 1964 and became the country of <a href="/wiki/Malta" title="Malta">Malta</a>, though the idea had been raised in 1955 of <a href="/wiki/1956_Maltese_United_Kingdom_integration_referendum" title="1956 Maltese United Kingdom integration referendum">integration with Britain</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-239"><a href="#cite_note-239">[239]</a></sup>
</p><p>Most of the UK's Caribbean territories achieved independence after the departure in 1961 and 1962 of Jamaica and Trinidad from the <a href="/wiki/West_Indies_Federation" title="West Indies Federation">West Indies Federation</a>, established in 1958 in an attempt to unite the British Caribbean colonies under one government, but which collapsed following the loss of its two largest members.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-knight14_240-0"><a href="#cite_note-knight14-240">[240]</a></sup> Jamaica attained independence in 1962, as did <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Trinidad and Tobago">Trinidad and Tobago</a>. Barbados achieved independence in 1966 and the remainder of the eastern Caribbean islands, including the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bahamas" title="Bahamas">Bahamas</a>, in the 1970s and 1980s,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-knight14_240-1"><a href="#cite_note-knight14-240">[240]</a></sup> but <a href="/wiki/Anguilla" title="Anguilla">Anguilla</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Turks_and_Caicos_Islands" title="Turks and Caicos Islands">Turks and Caicos Islands</a> opted to revert to British rule after they had already started on the path to independence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-241"><a href="#cite_note-241">[241]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/British_Virgin_Islands" title="British Virgin Islands">British Virgin Islands</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-242"><a href="#cite_note-242">[242]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Cayman_Islands" title="Cayman Islands">Cayman Islands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Montserrat" title="Montserrat">Montserrat</a> opted to retain ties with Britain,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-243"><a href="#cite_note-243">[243]</a></sup> while Guyana achieved independence in 1966. Britain's last colony on the American mainland, <a href="/wiki/British_Honduras" title="British Honduras">British Honduras</a>, became a self-governing colony in 1964 and was renamed <a href="/wiki/Belize" title="Belize">Belize</a> in 1973, achieving full independence in 1981. A <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Belizean-Guatemalan_territorial_dispute" title="Belizean-Guatemalan territorial dispute">dispute with Guatemala</a> over claims to Belize was left unresolved.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-244"><a href="#cite_note-244">[244]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/British_Overseas_Territories" title="British Overseas Territories">British Overseas Territories</a> in the Pacific acquired independence in the 1970s beginning with <a href="/wiki/Fiji" title="Fiji">Fiji</a> in 1970 and ending with <a href="/wiki/Vanuatu" title="Vanuatu">Vanuatu</a> in 1980. Vanuatu's independence was delayed because of political conflict between English and French-speaking communities, as the islands had been jointly administered as a <a href="/wiki/Condominium_(international_law)" title="Condominium (international law)">condominium</a> with France.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-245"><a href="#cite_note-245">[245]</a></sup> Fiji, <a href="/wiki/Papua_New_Guinea" title="Papua New Guinea">Papua New Guinea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Solomon_Islands" title="Solomon Islands">Solomon Islands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tuvalu" title="Tuvalu">Tuvalu</a> became <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_realm" title="Commonwealth realm">Commonwealth realms</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-246"><a href="#cite_note-246">[246]</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="End_of_empire">End of empire</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Falklands_War" title="Falklands War">Falklands War</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Transfer_of_sovereignty_over_Hong_Kong" title="Transfer of sovereignty over Hong Kong">Transfer of sovereignty over Hong Kong</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Patriation" title="Patriation">Patriation</a></div>
<p>By 1981, aside from a scattering of islands and outposts, the process of decolonisation that had begun after the Second World War was largely complete. In 1982, Britain's resolve in defending its remaining overseas territories was tested when <a href="/wiki/1982_invasion_of_the_Falkland_Islands" title="1982 invasion of the Falkland Islands">Argentina invaded the Falkland Islands</a>, acting on a long-standing claim that dated back to the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spanish Empire</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-247"><a href="#cite_note-247">[247]</a></sup> Britain's successful military response to retake the <a href="/wiki/Falkland_Islands" title="Falkland Islands">Falkland Islands</a> during the ensuing <a href="/wiki/Falklands_War" title="Falklands War">Falklands War</a> contributed to reversing the downward trend in Britain's status as a world power.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-248"><a href="#cite_note-248">[248]</a></sup>
</p><p>The 1980s saw Canada, Australia, and New Zealand sever their final constitutional links with Britain. Although granted legislative independence by the Statute of Westminster 1931, vestigial constitutional links had remained in place. The British Parliament retained the power to amend key Canadian constitutional statutes, meaning that effectively an act of the British Parliament was required to make certain changes to the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Canada" title="Constitution of Canada">Canadian Constitution</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-249"><a href="#cite_note-249">[249]</a></sup> The British Parliament had the power to pass laws extending to Canada at Canadian request. Although no longer able to pass any laws that would apply as Australian Commonwealth law, the British Parliament retained the power to legislate for the individual <a href="/wiki/States_and_territories_of_Australia" title="States and territories of Australia">Australian states</a>. With regard to New Zealand, the British Parliament retained the power to pass legislation applying to New Zealand with the <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand_Parliament" title="New Zealand Parliament">New Zealand Parliament</a>'s consent. In 1982, the last legal link between Canada and Britain was severed by the <a href="/wiki/Canada_Act_1982" title="Canada Act 1982">Canada Act 1982</a>, which was passed by the British parliament, formally <a href="/wiki/Patriation" title="Patriation">patriating</a> the Canadian Constitution. The act ended the need for British involvement in changes to the Canadian constitution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-refohbev594_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-refohbev594-9">[9]</a></sup> Similarly, the <a href="/wiki/Australia_Act_1986" title="Australia Act 1986">Australia Act 1986</a> (effective 3 March 1986) severed the constitutional link between Britain and the Australian states, while New Zealand's <a href="/wiki/Constitution_Act_1986" title="Constitution Act 1986">Constitution Act 1986</a> (effective 1 January 1987) reformed the constitution of New Zealand to sever its constitutional link with Britain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-250"><a href="#cite_note-250">[250]</a></sup>
</p><p>On 1 January 1984, Brunei, Britain's last remaining Asian protectorate, was granted independence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-251"><a href="#cite_note-251">[251]</a></sup> Independence had been delayed due to the opposition of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_sultans_of_Brunei" title="List of sultans of Brunei">Sultan</a>, who had preferred British protection.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-252"><a href="#cite_note-252">[252]</a></sup>
</p><p>In September 1982 the Prime Minister, <a href="/wiki/Margaret_Thatcher" title="Margaret Thatcher">Margaret Thatcher</a>, travelled to Beijing to negotiate with the Chinese Communist government, on the future of Britain's last major and most populous overseas territory, Hong Kong.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-253"><a href="#cite_note-253">[253]</a></sup> Under the terms of the 1842 <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Nanking" title="Treaty of Nanking">Treaty of Nanking</a> and 1860 <a href="/wiki/Convention_of_Peking" title="Convention of Peking">Convention of Peking</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong_Island" title="Hong Kong Island">Hong Kong Island</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kowloon_Peninsula" title="Kowloon Peninsula">Kowloon Peninsula</a> had been respectively ceded to Britain <i>in perpetuity</i>, but the majority of the colony consisted of the <a href="/wiki/New_Territories" title="New Territories">New Territories</a>, which had been acquired under a <a href="/wiki/Convention_for_the_Extension_of_Hong_Kong_Territory" title="Convention for the Extension of Hong Kong Territory">99-year lease in 1898</a>, due to expire in 1997.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-254"><a href="#cite_note-254">[254]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-255"><a href="#cite_note-255">[255]</a></sup> Thatcher, seeing parallels with the Falkland Islands, initially wished to hold Hong Kong and proposed British administration with Chinese sovereignty, though this was rejected by China.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-256"><a href="#cite_note-256">[256]</a></sup> A deal was reached in 1984—under the terms of the <a href="/wiki/Sino-British_Joint_Declaration" title="Sino-British Joint Declaration">Sino-British Joint Declaration</a>, Hong Kong would become a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Special_administrative_region_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="Special administrative region of the People's Republic of China">special administrative region of the People's Republic of China</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-257"><a href="#cite_note-257">[257]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong_handover_ceremony" title="Hong Kong handover ceremony">handover ceremony</a> in 1997 marked for many,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brendon-Empire-end_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-Brendon-Empire-end-8">[8]</a></sup> including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Charles,_Prince_of_Wales" title="Charles, Prince of Wales">Charles, Prince of Wales</a>, who was in attendance, "the end of Empire".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-refohbev594_9-2"><a href="#cite_note-refohbev594-9">[9]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy">Legacy</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/British_Overseas_Territories" title="British Overseas Territories">British Overseas Territories</a>, <a href="/wiki/English-speaking_world" title="English-speaking world">English-speaking world</a>, <a href="/wiki/Westminster_system" title="Westminster system">Westminster system</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Common_law" title="Common law">Common law</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Location_of_the_BOTs.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="433" data-file-width="735" decoding="async" height="130" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Location_of_the_BOTs.svg/220px-Location_of_the_BOTs.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Location_of_the_BOTs.svg/330px-Location_of_the_BOTs.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Location_of_the_BOTs.svg/440px-Location_of_the_BOTs.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Location_of_the_BOTs.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The fourteen <a href="/wiki/British_Overseas_Territories" title="British Overseas Territories">British Overseas Territories</a></div></div></div>
<p>Britain retains sovereignty over 14 territories outside the British Isles. In 1983, the <a href="/wiki/British_Nationality_Act_1981" title="British Nationality Act 1981">British Nationality Act 1981</a> renamed the existing <a href="/wiki/Crown_colony" title="Crown colony">Crown Colonies</a> as "British Dependent Territories",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-260"><a href="#cite_note-260">[note 1]</a></sup> and in 2002 they were renamed the <a href="/wiki/British_Overseas_Territories" title="British Overseas Territories">British Overseas Territories</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FAC_261-0"><a href="#cite_note-FAC-261">[260]</a></sup> Most former British colonies and protectorates are members of the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Voluntary_association" title="Voluntary association">voluntary association</a> of equal members, comprising a population of around 2.2 billion people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-262"><a href="#cite_note-262">[261]</a></sup> Fifteen Commonwealth realms voluntarily continue to share the British monarch, King Charles III, as their head of state. These fifteen nations are distinct and equal legal entities – the <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Monarchy of the United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Australia" title="Monarchy of Australia">Australia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Canada" title="Monarchy of Canada">Canada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_New_Zealand" title="Monarchy of New Zealand">New Zealand</a>, <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Antigua_and_Barbuda" title="Monarchy of Antigua and Barbuda">Antigua and Barbuda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_the_Bahamas" title="Monarchy of the Bahamas">The Bahamas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Belize" title="Monarchy of Belize">Belize</a>, <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Grenada" title="Monarchy of Grenada">Grenada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Jamaica" title="Monarchy of Jamaica">Jamaica</a>, <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Papua_New_Guinea" title="Monarchy of Papua New Guinea">Papua New Guinea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis" title="Monarchy of Saint Kitts and Nevis">Saint Kitts and Nevis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Saint_Lucia" title="Monarchy of Saint Lucia">Saint Lucia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines" title="Monarchy of Saint Vincent and the Grenadines">Saint Vincent and the Grenadines</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_the_Solomon_Islands" title="Monarchy of the Solomon Islands">Solomon Islands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Tuvalu" title="Monarchy of Tuvalu">Tuvalu</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-263"><a href="#cite_note-263">[262]</a></sup>
</p><p>Decades, and in some cases centuries, of British rule and emigration have left their mark on the independent nations that arose from the British Empire. The empire established the use of the <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English language</a> in regions around the world. Today it is the primary language of up to 460 million people and is spoken by about 1.5 billion as a first, second or foreign language.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-264"><a href="#cite_note-264">[263]</a></sup> Individual and team sports developed in Britain, particularly <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cricket" title="Cricket">cricket</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lawn_tennis" title="Lawn tennis">lawn tennis</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Golf" title="Golf">golf</a> were exported.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-265"><a href="#cite_note-265">[264]</a></sup> British <a href="/wiki/Missionary" title="Missionary">missionaries</a> who travelled around the globe often in advance of soldiers and civil servants spread <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestantism</a> (including <a href="/wiki/Anglicanism" title="Anglicanism">Anglicanism</a>) to all continents. The British Empire provided refuge for religiously persecuted continental Europeans for hundreds of years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-266"><a href="#cite_note-266">[265]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%81%E0%B4%9F%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%9F%E0%B4%BF%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%BE_%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%B0%E0%B4%BF%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%95%E0%B4%B1%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%B1%E0%B5%8D_%E0%B4%95%E0%B4%B3%E0%B4%BF%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%81%E0%B4%A8%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%A8%E0%B5%81.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1294" data-file-width="1194" decoding="async" height="184" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%81%E0%B4%9F%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%9F%E0%B4%BF%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%BE_%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%B0%E0%B4%BF%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%95%E0%B4%B1%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%B1%E0%B5%8D_%E0%B4%95%E0%B4%B3%E0%B4%BF%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%81%E0%B4%A8%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%A8%E0%B5%81.jpg/170px-%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%81%E0%B4%9F%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%9F%E0%B4%BF%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%BE_%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%B0%E0%B4%BF%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%95%E0%B4%B1%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%B1%E0%B5%8D_%E0%B4%95%E0%B4%B3%E0%B4%BF%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%81%E0%B4%A8%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%A8%E0%B5%81.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%81%E0%B4%9F%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%9F%E0%B4%BF%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%BE_%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%B0%E0%B4%BF%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%95%E0%B4%B1%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%B1%E0%B5%8D_%E0%B4%95%E0%B4%B3%E0%B4%BF%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%81%E0%B4%A8%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%A8%E0%B5%81.jpg/255px-%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%81%E0%B4%9F%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%9F%E0%B4%BF%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%BE_%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%B0%E0%B4%BF%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%95%E0%B4%B1%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%B1%E0%B5%8D_%E0%B4%95%E0%B4%B3%E0%B4%BF%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%81%E0%B4%A8%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%A8%E0%B5%81.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%81%E0%B4%9F%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%9F%E0%B4%BF%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%BE_%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%B0%E0%B4%BF%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%95%E0%B4%B1%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%B1%E0%B5%8D_%E0%B4%95%E0%B4%B3%E0%B4%BF%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%81%E0%B4%A8%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%A8%E0%B5%81.jpg/340px-%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%81%E0%B4%9F%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%9F%E0%B4%BF%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%BE_%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%B0%E0%B4%BF%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%95%E0%B4%B1%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%B1%E0%B5%8D_%E0%B4%95%E0%B4%B3%E0%B4%BF%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%81%E0%B4%A8%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%A8%E0%B5%81.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%81%E0%B4%9F%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%9F%E0%B4%BF%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%BE_%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%B0%E0%B4%BF%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%95%E0%B4%B1%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%B1%E0%B5%8D_%E0%B4%95%E0%B4%B3%E0%B4%BF%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%81%E0%B4%A8%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%A8%E0%B5%81.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Cricket" title="Cricket">Cricket</a> being played in <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>. Sports developed in Britain or the former empire continue to be viewed and played.</div></div></div>
<p>Political boundaries drawn by the British did not always reflect homogeneous ethnicities or religions, contributing to conflicts in formerly colonised areas. The British Empire was responsible for large migrations of peoples. Millions left the <a href="/wiki/British_Isles" title="British Isles">British Isles</a>, with the founding <a href="/wiki/Settler_colonialism" title="Settler colonialism">settler colonist</a> populations of the United States, Canada, Australia and New Zealand coming mainly from Britain and Ireland. Tensions remain between the white settler populations of these countries and their indigenous minorities, and between white settler minorities and indigenous majorities in South Africa and Zimbabwe. Settlers in <a href="/wiki/Ireland" title="Ireland">Ireland</a> from Great Britain have left their mark in the form of divided <a href="/wiki/Irish_nationalism" title="Irish nationalism">nationalist</a> and <a href="/wiki/Unionism_in_Ireland" title="Unionism in Ireland">unionist</a> communities in Northern Ireland. Millions of people moved to and from British colonies, with large numbers of <a href="/wiki/Non-resident_Indian_and_Overseas_Citizen_of_India" title="Non-resident Indian and Overseas Citizen of India">Overseas Indian</a> people emigrating to other parts of the empire, such as Malaysia and Fiji, and <a href="/wiki/Overseas_Chinese" title="Overseas Chinese">Overseas Chinese</a> people to Malaysia, Singapore and the Caribbean.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-267"><a href="#cite_note-267">[266]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Demography_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Demography of the United Kingdom">demographics of the United Kingdom</a> itself were changed after the Second World War owing to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Immigration_to_the_United_Kingdom_since_1922#Post-war_immigration_(1945–1983)" title="Immigration to the United Kingdom since 1922">immigration to Britain</a> from its former colonies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-268"><a href="#cite_note-268">[267]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the 19th century, <a href="/wiki/List_of_British_innovations_and_discoveries" title="List of British innovations and discoveries">innovation in Britain</a> led to revolutionary changes in manufacturing, the development of <a href="/wiki/Factory_system" title="Factory system">factory systems</a>, and the growth of transportation by railway and steamship.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-269"><a href="#cite_note-269">[268]</a></sup> British colonial architecture, such as in churches, railway stations and government buildings, can be seen in many cities that were once part of the British Empire.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-270"><a href="#cite_note-270">[269]</a></sup> The British choice of system of measurement, the <a href="/wiki/Imperial_units" title="Imperial units">imperial system</a>, continues to be used in some countries in various ways. The convention of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Right-_and_left-hand_traffic" title="Right- and left-hand traffic">driving on the left-hand side of the road</a> has been retained in much of the former empire.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-271"><a href="#cite_note-271">[270]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Westminster_system" title="Westminster system">Westminster system</a> of <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_system" title="Parliamentary system">parliamentary democracy</a> has served as the template for the governments for many former colonies,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-272"><a href="#cite_note-272">[271]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-273"><a href="#cite_note-273">[272]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/English_law" title="English law">English common law</a> for legal systems.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2004b307_274-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2004b307-274">[273]</a></sup> International commercial contracts are often based on English common law.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-275"><a href="#cite_note-275">[274]</a></sup> The British <a href="/wiki/Judicial_Committee_of_the_Privy_Council" title="Judicial Committee of the Privy Council">Judicial Committee of the Privy Council</a> still serves as the highest court of appeal for twelve former colonies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-276"><a href="#cite_note-276">[275]</a></sup>
</p><p>Historians' <a href="/wiki/Historiography_of_the_British_Empire" title="Historiography of the British Empire">approaches to understanding the British Empire</a> are diverse and evolving.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-winks_277-0"><a href="#cite_note-winks-277">[276]</a></sup> Two key sites of debate over recent decades have been the impact of <a href="/wiki/Postcolonialism" title="Postcolonialism">post-colonial studies</a>, which seek to <a href="/wiki/Critical_theory" title="Critical theory">critically</a> re-evaluate the history of imperialism, and the continued relevance of historians <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Robinson" title="Ronald Robinson">Ronald Robinson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jack_Gallagher_(historian)" title="Jack Gallagher (historian)">John Gallagher</a>, whose work greatly influenced imperial historiography during the 1950s and 1960s. In addition, differing assessments of the empire's legacy remain relevant to debates over recent history and politics, such as the Anglo-American <a href="/wiki/2003_invasion_of_Iraq" title="2003 invasion of Iraq">invasions of Iraq</a> and <a href="/wiki/United_States_invasion_of_Afghanistan" title="United States invasion of Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a>, as well as Britain's role and identity in the contemporary world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-278"><a href="#cite_note-278">[277]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mitter_279-0"><a href="#cite_note-mitter-279">[278]</a></sup>
</p><p>Historians such as <a href="/wiki/Caroline_Elkins" title="Caroline Elkins">Caroline Elkins</a> have argued against perceptions of the British Empire as a primarily liberalising and modernising enterprise, criticising its widespread use of violence and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Emergency_law" title="Emergency law">emergency laws</a> to maintain power.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mitter_279-1"><a href="#cite_note-mitter-279">[278]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-280"><a href="#cite_note-280">[279]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2022)">page needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Common criticisms of the empire include the use of detention camps in its colonies, massacres of <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples" title="Indigenous peoples">indigenous peoples</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_281-0"><a href="#cite_note-:1-281">[280]</a></sup> and famine-response policies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-282"><a href="#cite_note-282">[281]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_283-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-283">[282]</a></sup> Some scholars, including <a href="/wiki/Amartya_Sen" title="Amartya Sen">Amartya Sen</a>, assert that British policies worsened the <a href="/wiki/Famine_in_India" title="Famine in India">famines in India</a> that killed millions during British rule.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-amartyasen_284-0"><a href="#cite_note-amartyasen-284">[283]</a></sup> Conversely, historians such as <a href="/wiki/Niall_Ferguson" title="Niall Ferguson">Niall Ferguson</a> say that the economic and institutional development the British Empire brought resulted in a net benefit to its colonies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-285"><a href="#cite_note-285">[284]</a></sup> Other historians treat its legacy as varied and ambiguous.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mitter_279-2"><a href="#cite_note-mitter-279">[278]</a></sup> Public attitudes towards the empire within Britain remain somewhat positive.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_283-1"><a href="#cite_note-:0-283">[282]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-286"><a href="#cite_note-286">[285]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span></h2>

<li id="cite_note-260"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-260">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Schedule 6 of the <a href="/wiki/British_Nationality_Act_1981" title="British Nationality Act 1981">British Nationality Act 1981</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-258"><a href="#cite_note-258">[258]</a></sup> reclassified the remaining Crown colonies as "British Dependent Territories".  The Act entered into force on 1 January 1983<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-259"><a href="#cite_note-259">[259]</a></sup></span>
